## FILE: Basic Facts.md

---
title: Basic Patient Facts
type: summary
created: 2026-04-06
updated: 2026-04-06
sources: []
tags: [patient, background]
confidence: subjective
---

Rafael Lino
Born 1989 
Has Portuguese and Brazilian Dual citizenship 
Has UK EU Settled Citizen visa giving him indefinite leave to remain. 

I have bipolar disorder, diagnosed since 2017-18. 

Initially took Seroquel SR (quetiapine) and Lamictal (lamotrigine). Seroquel dose fluctuated between 300mg and 600mg daily for years between 2018-2022 due to seasonal variation of the bipolar condition. 

Had a bunch of weird symptoms after COVID Vaccine in August 2021. 

Had to be removed from Seroquel / Quetiapine in 2022 due to unknown motor symptoms, at the time described as parkinsonism, which at the time seen as drug-induced (quetiapine related) and gradual loss of memory. This was progressive but really got much worse and critical in late 2022. Quetiapine was reduced to 100mg and Lithium was introduced at 600-800mg. Lamotrigine was removed. By the end of this episode it was hard to walk around and memory was reduced to 5-30min. But right after removal of the quetiapine, I improved fast. Memory and motor function was mostly after 3 days, pretty normal in 1 week.

Some signs of the motor dysfunction remained, though much diminished. 

Due to crisis in the audiovisual sector, I moved back with my mother near the end of 2023, and became her full time carer. She had depression and a seeming loss of cognitive function. 

In late 2024 and progressing to 2025 some fatigue appeared. This worsened towards late 2025, and was left unexplained. By the end of 2025 and start of 2026, due to salt loading improving fatigue a lot, an investigation was started in suspected autonomic dysfunction. 

I spoke to multiple doctors, including cardiologists in the Uk, one of whom said they had seen this before in post vaccine syndrome. However, the reappearance of motor dysfunction and a "cauda equina" like episode of loss of sensitivity in the saddle area and genitalia led to a neurologist assessment of Functional Neurological Syndrome. This is alongside documented polyuria and still suspected autonomic dysfunction. A recent - March 2026 - ECG Stress Test showed loss of function. Yet in 2025 summer I was doing one kettlebell mile a day with between 16kg and 24kg, and I made a feature film which required long working hours.

## FILE: README.md

# Health-LLM

My Health files for helping with the diagnostic of an unknown neurological disease.

This is an Obsidian vault. You should run it under Obsidian so you can navigate it in the way it was initially designed. It can also be quickly read and navigated through an llm assistant. 



Thanks to Andrej Karpathy for the idea.

Mostly executed with Anthropics Claude Code and Claude.

## FILE: Self Exams and Logs/Personal Log - March 2026 Update.md

---
title: Personal Log — March 2026
type: timeline
created: 2026-03-01
updated: 2026-04-06
sources: []
tags: [symptoms, log]
confidence: subjective
---

**Diário de Saude  

  

Started 11.03.2026

  

Medicação Inicial - 2022-2025:

Lítio 600mg

Seroquel 50mg 

  

Suplementos:

Nenhums

  

Níveis de energia:

Normais com estranhas faltas de energia em Março

3-4 horas de fadiga extrema em Setembro 2025

Dificuldade em sair da cama / sofá em Janeiro 2026

Recuperação rápida com suplementação de 4-6g de sal dissolvido em água - dividido em 2x ou 3x doses por dia. Inicialmente 2g sal em 400ml de água, depois reduzido para 2g sal em 200ml de água. 

  

Relato: 

  

Em Março de 2025 ano tinha dias contínuos a trabalhar sem grandes problemas.

Pelo Verão de 2025 já tinha fadiga acentuada e estratégias de compensação. Recuperava com exercício e 1-2 horas de luz solar (fazia exercício ao ar livre). No Verão fiz bastante caminhadas com peso, caminhava 1.5km com 16 a 24kg adicionados, sendo o meu peso na altura 80kg. Sentia que o Sol + exercício ajudava. Existia alguma fadiga, estranha. Inicialmente associei os sintomas ao bipolar. Acabou por ser difícil manter esta associação após Janeiro de 2026, com a introdução de 4-6g de sal dissolvido em água em 2x a 3x doses diárias, e a resolução praticamente imediata (40-90min.) da fadiga - e da raiva inexplicada até então. 

  

Setembro de 2026 (est.) 

  

Comecei a tomar magnésio e Vitamina D quando foi primeiro detectado a sua potencial ausência num teste de sangue feito pelo laboratório Germano de Sousa (que era mínima mas decidi precaver). Estava a fazer testes em coordenação com o meu Psiquiatra para investigar a razão para a fadiga e falta de energia que me vinha a afligir desde 2024. 

  

A introdução de suplementos de magnésio e Vitamina D por volta de Setembro de 2025 parece colmatar o que se passava. Senti-me, durante algum tempo, bastante melhor. 

  

Isto foi por volta de Setembro de 2025. Registado em email com o meu Psiquiatra.

  

Estimo na altura 266mg de magnésio e 8000 IU de Vitamina D - Doses Diárias. São ambos os suplementos da Solgar. 

  

A fadiga por volta desta altura já é bastante acentuada. Isto significa, já em Setembro/Outubro, talvez 3 a 4 horas passados em cama a recuperar. Depois de passar algum tempo (45 min a 1 hora) na cama, recuperava, continuava a trabalhar. Com os suplementos, isto reduz-se, mas não desaparece. E gradualmente, os suplementos perdem eficácia, embora isso só se torne óbvio em Janeiro de 2026. 

  

Tinha também a questão da raiva. A partir de certa hora, sentia uma “mudança” e havia uma alteração na minha capacidade de tolerar as coisas. Inicialmente achei que a raiva poderia ter alguma relação com a bipolaridade. Mas era “diferente”, vinha em certa hora, sentia “pressão” a subir pela espinha até à parte de trás da cabeça. E a partir dessa hora, era díficil “esquecer” qualquer coisa que me irritava. A pressão na cabeça estava alterada, sentia isso fisicamente. Havia pressão à volta da parte de cima da cabeça, pela testa e pela região nesta zona, pela parte de trás da cabeça e pela parte de trás do pescoço. Era como uma ativação. E sentia que algo químico se tinha alterado, e a partir desse ponto as coisas só pioravam - era difícil lidar com qualquer desafio sem algum descontrolo. Estava sempre no limite. Conseguia isolar-me e trabalhar pois trabalho remotamente.  
  
Como os ataques de raiva pareciam-me subir em número e gravidade quando tirava o Seroquel, mantive-o em conjunto com o lítio. Ou seja, desde 2022 ( e da crise distônica que levou ao abandono como fármaco principal ) a medicação ficou igual, com algumas tentativas de sair do Seroquel apenas, que depois de 2022 estava também apenas em 50mg.*

  

Durante grande parte deste tempo, a combinação de raiva + fadiga fez-me pensar que isto se tratava de uma questão relacionada com o bipolar, com depressão bipolar e raiva bipolar.

  

Contudo a introdução de água com sal em Janeiro de 2026 remove os 2 problemas - comprovados com tanto redução da fadiga, como também é eficaz em “acabar” com um ataque de raiva. Questiona-se assim a relação com a bipolaridade, pois não vejo razão para a bipolaridade ser afetada por ingestão de água com sal. 

  

Vou para o Brazil em Dezembro. Fadiga/baixa energia continua. Suplementação parece reduzir o problema, mas não o resolve.  

  

* Registo Histórico: Medicação 2018-2022 - Seroquel SR - 300mg - Lamictal / Lamotrigina - não me recordo bem da dose, mas talvez 150mg. Alterado para Lítio 600mg e Seroquel 50mg após crise distônica. 

  

Dezembro/Janeiro 2026

  

No Brazil fico sem os suplementos. Durante algum tempo parece-me ok. Parece-me que no Brazil, onde é Verão, e há sol, e estou de férias. 

Mas eventualmente os sintomas retornam e fico sem suplementos Solgar que trouxe comigo de Portugal, vou e compro Magnésio e Vitamina D localmente. Talvez de baixa qualidade.

Sinto melhoria também a tomar água de coco - em conjunto com os suplementos. Não sei se é coincidência ou útil, mas pareceu-me que me fazia bem na altura.

  

Certamente os suplementos não são tão eficazes, mas consigo trabalhar. 

  

Retorno a Portugal em Janeiro 2026

  

Poucos dias após o retorno os sintomas agravam-se. Estou no meu pior estado. A maior parte do dia é no sofá ou na cama a descansar. Fico com preocupação sobre manter o meu emprego. A situação torna-se grave o suficiente que já não sei como me manter útil. A maior parte das horas do dia estou a recuperar ou a tentar recuperar. 

  

Reparo que quando me sento fico pior ainda. Parece que vou adormecer. Transformo a minha secretária numa standing desk para conseguir continuar a trabalhar. 

  

Mais grave: quando vou fazer exercício (pela primeira vez vou ao exterior fazer exercício em meses, devido à chuva), sinto que vou adormecer ou ter um blackout. Volto para casa. É aí que, numa tentativa de perceber o que se passa, (já não tolero exercício) faço pesquisas sobre a minha condição - e uma sugestão aparece - tomar sal dissolvido em água. 2g em 400ml. 

  

Faço isso. Tomo 2g de sal em 400ml, tudo duma vez em 2-3 min. e o meu cansaço desaparece em uma hora. Diria que em 60 min. estou funcional. Em 15-30 min. já senti uma diferença enorme. 

  

Pouco depois continuo a pesquisar. A raiva pode ser cortisol. Faço o teste. Deixo aparecer um episódio de raiva (na altura ainda comuns). Tomo o sal diretamente em cima do episódio. Ele desaparece. 

  

Tanto a raiva quanto o cansaço são diretamente afetados pela introdução do Sal. 

  
  

Fim de Janeiro 2026  

  

Formulei por volta desta altura um plano mais agressivo de suplementação.

  

De fim de Janeiro 2026 até 8 de Março 2026 - Doses Diárias

Pure EPA Omega 3 - 1000mg 

Fairvital B2 - Vitamin B2 - 93mg + L-leucin - 120 mg 

Calcium citrate - 1000mg - calcium 

Bysglicinato de magnésio - 900mg 

Magnesium L-Threonate - 500mg 

Vitamin D3 (essential nutrition) - 6000 IU 

Vitamin D3/K2 Combinado - Vitamina D3 2000 IU / Vitamina K2 100ug 

Magnésio que Dissolve do Pingo Doce - 375mg 

Vitamina C - 1000mg 

2x  sacos de Dioralyte - Glicose 3.56 - Cloreto de sódio 0.47 - Cloreto de potássio 0.30  - 6 Citrato dissodico 0.53 (2x ao dia)

CoQ10 - 400mg 

E 6 gramas de sal. Inicialmente dissolvidos em 400ml. Depois em 200ml quando é encontrada a poliúria nos exames de urina (4.3L e 5.6L). 

USADOS MAS INTERROMPIDOS

Vitamin B12 - Methylcobalamin - 1000mg

Tomei 2-3 dias mas parei. Fez-me sentir “estranho” e tive uma má sensação. Logo interrompido. 

  

NAC - 600 to 300mg - maior parte dos dias 300mg

Sim e não durante 2-3 semanas e depois interrompido. 

Por volta da mesma altura, com alguma confiança e querendo reduzir um fármaco que creio ter-me criado problemas anteriormente - removo o Seroquel completamente, com conhecimento do meu psiquiatra. 

  

Nova Crise Distônica 

  

Estamos no início de Março.

A fadiga parece estar a reduzir a intensidade.

Como se ao “repor os níveis”, o corpo parece estar a recuperar.

É difícil de dizer pois não interrompo o Sal diário de 4-6g. 

Mas sinto que em Janeiro, a fadiga que tinha entre tomas de sal era desestabilizante. 

No Carnaval no Porto, 22 de Fevereiro, tive problemas com atividade física continuada. Andar pela rua durante várias horas levou a uma reposição de sal de +2g. 

Mas pelo ínicio de Março, a fadiga torna-se menos e menos presente entre as tomas de sal. 

Os sintomas continuam lá mas menos presentes. 

  

Contudo, um novo sintoma apresenta-se - a distonia, que causou a crise em 2022, parece estar a voltar.* Não consigo explicar. Lembro-me de tomar sal na primeira semana de Março porque acredito que a distonia pode ser “fadiga disfarçada” e exagero um pouco no sal porque acredito que tenho de evitar a fadiga, e que a distonia deve ser um alerta que A. o corpo está mais estável B. que a distonia e fadiga devem estar de alguma maneira associadas. 

  

* Na realidade a distonia nunca desapareceu desde 2022, mas a sua presença era muito muito pouco acentuada. A partir da primeira semana de Março, volta com uma força que não existia desde 2022. Há uma marcada progressão e agravamento dos sintomas de distonia que eram mínimos até então. 

  

9 de Março de 2026

Em 9 de Março de 2026 há nova crise distônica. 

Semelhante, de todas as maneiras, com a crise de 2022 - mas apresenta também sintomas de 2021. 

A progressão culminou num episódio grave  — movimentos involuntários violentos nos braços e mãos, ardor e formigueiro na parte de trás e nas laterais da cabeça e uma sensação generalizada que só posso descrever como o meu corpo «em chamas», particularmente na parte de trás da cabeça e também nos impulsos em torno dos movimentos do meu corpo — várias coisas a acontecerem ao mesmo tempo, demais para suportar. 

Este episódio pareceu idêntico ou muito semelhante em caráter a algumas das minhas apresentações pós-vacina originais de 2021 + sintomas dos eventos de distonia de 2022. 

  

Nota: O episódio de distonia aguda de 2022 ocorreu com Seroquel 300 mg e lamotrigina e foi atribuído ao medicamento - tenho o relatório do hospital a confirmar isso e um vídeo do que aconteceu. 

Continuei então com uma dose baixa de Seroquel (50-25 mg) durante aproximadamente 3 anos. Pouco antes deste episódio, interrompo completamente os últimos 25 mg há apenas algumas semanas. 

  

Desde a interrupção do Seroquel (que foi acompanhada também pela alteração nos suplementos, por exemplo a introdução de mais magnésio), a distonia reapareceu progressivamente e piorou ao longo de várias semanas.

  
  

Sobre a distonia ,

 observei o seguinte:

∙ A distonia não está presente pela manhã, após acordar.

∙ Ela começa à tarde e piora ao longo da noite.

∙ Esse padrão tem sido consistente ao longo dos dias, tanto antes quanto depois do episódio grave.

∙ Deitar proporciona um alívio parcial.

∙ Retomei o Seroquel 50 mg proporcionou um alívio significativo ontem. Também tomei 20 mg de cetirizina, pois fazia parte da minha recuperação pós-covid (isso fazia parte do pacote de suplementos da Front Line Covid Care Alliance que tomei em 2021 para melhorar os meus sintomas). 

  

Outros Sintomas adicionais atuais:

∙ Dor intermitente no escroto e dor acima dos genitais (isto acontece há mais de um mês)

  
  

Novo plano de suplementação: 

  

Assustado pelos resultados e pela crise distônica (que achei antes tinha sido resolvida) alterei o plano de suplementação: 

  

Vitamin D3 (essential nutrition) - 4000 IU 

Vitamin D3/K2 Combinado - Vitamina D3 2000 IU / Vitamina K2 100ug 

Magnesium L-Threonate - 1000mg 

Pure EPA Omega 3 - 1000mg 

2x  sacos de Dioralyte

E 2 gramas de sal dissolvidos em 200ml 3x ao dia. 

  

No dia da crise distônica: 

20mg de cetirizina 

E 50mg de Seroquel (que já não tomava há semanas)

  

Nos dias a seguir adiciono

Telfast 180mg de manhã

20mg Famotidina pela noite

A seguir a combinação que me ajudou em 2021. 

  

Exames BP/HR

Supine (lying down ~10 minutes)  
• Reading 1: ~104 / 65, HR 57  
• Reading 2: ~103 / 64, HR 56

Standing test  
• 1 minuto: 103 / 66, HR 71  
• ~4–5 minutos: 107 / 69, HR 69  
• 10 minutos: 109 / 71, HR 71

Mais tarde quando os sintomas aparecem e tornam se óbvios 

 • 96 / 60, HR 66

Episódio sintomático depois de comer  
• ~101 / 67, HR 72

  

Log de Urina 

24 February 2026 - 1a urina - 1.7L 

08/04/2026 - 1a urina - 1.4L  - No night time urine - didn’t wake up to pee 

09/04/2026 - 1a urina - 1L - No night time urine - didn’t wake up to pee

  

13 Março 2026

  

Urina praticamente branca / transparente 

(Devia ter cor antes porque tomava B2) 

Sem sensação no perineo 

Numb 

  

14 Março 

03.00am 

Scrotum pain quite bad

Always seems to get worse at night in bed (?)**

### ER Visit #1 — Discharge + Bloods
```yaml
type: Emergency Department — Discharge Note + Blood Panel
date: 2021-08-20
lab: Germano de Sousa (via Hospital CUF Porto)
location: Hospital CUF Porto
symptoms: Altered sensation right hemibody (onset day before), now asymptomatic
```
- **Transcript:** [Notas-de-Alta-2021-08-20](../../Transcripts%20Anonymous/2021/08-August/Discharge-Notes/Notas-de-Alta-2021-08-20.md) | [Resultados-Patologia-Clinica-2021-08-20](../../Transcripts%20Anonymous/2021/08-August/Lab-Results/Resultados-Patologia-Clinica-2021-08-20.md)
- **Remarkable results:**
  - D-Dimer **elevated** at 1264.74 ng/ml (ref <500)
  - CRP mildly elevated at 6.335 mg/L (ref <5)
  - LDH elevated at 224 U/L (ref 40-207)
  - Platelets borderline low at 139 (ref 150-400)
  - Troponin normal — cardiac injury ruled out
- **Follow-up:** Returned to ER on 22/08, 23/08, and 25/08

---

### ER Visit #3 — Neurology Assessment
```yaml
type: Emergency Department — Neurology Consultation
date: 2021-08-23
location: Hospital CUF Porto
symptoms: Continuation of right hemibody numbness, weakness, muscle spasms (day 4-6 post-vaccine)
```

## Reference

### I-RECOVER Protocol — Personal Account
```yaml
type: Personal Narrative — Post-Vaccine Treatment
date: 2021 (August–September)
location: N/A — self-authored
symptoms: Post-Janssen vaccine: right hemibody sensory loss, arm weakness, muscle spasms, tremors, "lightning flash" nerve pain, headaches
```
- **Transcript:** [I-RECOVER-Protocol-Personal-Account-2021](../../Transcripts%20Anonymous/2021/Reference/I-RECOVER-Protocol-Personal-Account-2021.md)
- **Key points:**
  - Day 1–3 post-vaccine: normal headaches
  - Day 4: right hemibody sensory loss, CT clean
  - Day 5: right arm weakness, muscle spasms, hospitalisation
  - 1 month of tremors, weakness, nerve pain; alcohol worsens symptoms
  - **Self-treatment via I-RECOVER protocol:** Niacin 100mg, Vitamin C 1500mg, Vitamin D 3000IU, Zinc 15mg, Selenium 50mcg, Quercetin 500mg, Aspirin 100mg
  - Antihistamine and mast cell approach provided gradual improvement

---

## Summary of 2021 Key Findings

| Finding | Status |
|---|---|
| Pre-vaccine baseline: no COVID antibodies, normal D-dimer, lymphocytosis already present | Established April + August 2021 |
| Right hemibody sensory/motor symptoms post-Janssen vaccine (Aug 2021) | Investigated extensively — no structural cause found |
| D-dimer spike: normal (239) → elevated (1264) within 24h of symptom onset | Private tracking documents rapid onset |
| D-dimer trajectory: 239→1264→478→458→519→599→1284→548→244 | Resolved by Nov 2021; no PE or DVT on imaging |
| Brain lesion — 6mm neuroglial cyst, right lingual gyrus | Stable on follow-up MRI (June 2022) |
| Left occipital condyle vascular malformation (16x14mm) | Confirmed as vascular fenestration, no pathological significance |
| COVID PCR negative (Aug 2021) — symptoms vaccine-related, not COVID | Confirmed |
| Persistent mild thrombocytopenia (139–157) | Ongoing pattern |
| Persistent mild lymphocytosis (40–44%) | Pre-dates vaccine (42.7% in April); ongoing pattern |
| Left chest pain post-vaccine | CT angio normal, no PE, no myocarditis on CT |
| Stopped Lamictal due to post-vaccine fatigue | Authorised by psychiatrist; restarted later |
| Self-treatment with I-RECOVER protocol + antihistamines | Gradual improvement reported |

### Sleep Study — Polysomnography
```yaml
type: Sleep Study — Nocturnal Polysomnography (Full PSG)
date: 2022-01-20
lab: Centro de Medicina do Sono
location: Hospital CUF Porto
symptoms: Investigation of sleep-disordered breathing (context of post-vaccine fatigue and neurological symptoms)
```
- **Transcripts:** [Registo-Poligrafico-Sono-2022-01-20](../../Transcripts%20Anonymous/2022/01-January/Sleep-Study/Registo-Poligrafico-Sono-2022-01-20.md) | [Polysomnography-Data-Report-2022-01-20](../../Transcripts%20Anonymous/2022/01-January/Sleep-Study/Polysomnography-Data-Report-2022-01-20.md)
- **Remarkable results:**
  - **Mild obstructive sleep apnoea — AHI = 7/h** (3 obstructive, 2 central, 55 hypopnoeas)
  - Predominantly in REM sleep (REM RDI 15.8 vs NREM RDI 5.5), no positional factor
  - Sleep efficiency 97.1%, sleep latency very short at 2.1 min
  - **Deep slow-wave sleep and REM sleep percentages decreased**
  - Sleep fragmentation noted — total arousal index 13.9/h (mainly hypopnoea arousals)
  - Min SpO2 = 89%, mean SpO2 = 94%, ODI = 2/h
  - Heart rate: mean 68.5 bpm, min 26.5 bpm (during sleep), max 135.9 bpm — **no arrhythmias**
  - No significant periodic limb movements (PLMS index 0)
- **Follow-up:** CPAP therapy initiated

  - Examined jointly with neurology
  - **CK normal at 207** (ref 39-308) — no rhabdomyolysis
  - ECG: no rhythm/conduction disturbances, QT normal
  - Platelets improved to 176 (best value)

  - Reports symptom recurrence with lower doses of Quetiapine
- **Diagnosis:** 33372 - **Acute dystonia due to drugs**
- **Follow-up:** Started Artane; referred to treating psychiatrist (appointment 15/11); later switched from quetiapine to lithium

| Finding | Status |
|---|---|

| **Lithium critically low** (0.23–0.29 mmol/l) | Worst levels recorded; renal wasting suspected |
| **Severe polyuria** (3300–5600 ml/24h) | Progressive; suggests renal concentrating defect |
| **Urinary iron very low** (9.9 µg/24h) | Markedly below range |
| Vitamin D insufficient (24 ng/ml) | Supplementation started with improvement |
| Progressive fatigue throughout year | Worsening from summer; partially responsive to Mg + Vit D supplementation |
| **Salt supplementation provides dramatic relief** | Discovered Jan 2026 — complete symptom resolution within 30–40 min |
| No ER visits or imaging in 2025 | Outpatient monitoring; critical deterioration developing |

### Exercise Stress Test (Prova de Esforço — ECG)
```yaml
type: Cardiology — Exercise ECG Stress Test
date: 2026-03-13
location: Hospital A (Porto) — Cardiologista B / Cardiologista C
symptoms: Chronic fatigue, exercise intolerance, suspected autonomic dysfunction
```
- **Transcript:** [Prova-de-Esforco-ECG-2026-03-13](../../Transcripts%20Anonymous/2026/03-March/Cardiology-Tests/Prova-de-Esforco-ECG-2026-03-13.md)
- **Remarkable results:**
  - Baseline: HR 76 bpm, BP 166/70 mmHg
  - Peak: HR **117 bpm (only 63% of predicted max)** — insufficient chronotropic response
  - BP **dropped to 110/64** during exercise — **discordant haemodynamic response**
  - Test duration: **4 min 26 sec** — terminated early (fatigue, near-syncope)
  - Recovery required Trendelenburg position + subcutaneous glucagon
  - No rhythm changes or arrhythmias
- **Context:** **Objectively abnormal exercise response** — reduced functional capacity, chronotropic incompetence, exercise-induced hypotension; consistent with dysautonomia

---

## Summary of 2026 Key Findings

| Finding | Status |
|---|---|
| **Minerals recovering** with supplementation (Ca, Mg normalised by Jan–Feb) | Salt + Vitamin D + Mg supplementation effective |
| **Lithium volatile** (0.25→0.56 within weeks) | Renal wasting confirmed; levels track inversely with urine output |
| **Polyuria improving** (5600→4350→2620 ml/24h by March) | Renal concentrating defect; responding to salt loading |
| **Zinc depletion** (61 ��g/dl) | Below range; part of mineral wasting pattern |
| **Exercise stress test: objectively abnormal** | 63% predicted HR, exercise hypotension, 4.5 min duration |
| **ANA negative, tryptase normal, complement normal** | Rules out systemic autoimmunity and MCAS |
| **HPA axis normal** (cortisol, ACTH) | No adrenal insufficiency |
| **RAAS borderline** (renin at upper limit) | Possible compensatory activation from polyuria/salt loss |
| **FND diagnosis** by Neurologist C (London) | Whole neuraxis MRI planned for April |
| **Dysautonomia suspected** by Cardiologist A (London) | Under active investigation |
| **Dystonia/movement disorder recurrence** (March 2026) | Previously documented as drug-induced (2022); now recurring off causative agent |

## FILE: Sublinks/Important Start Notes and Current Observations.md

---
title: Important Start Notes
type: summary
created: 2026-03-01
updated: 2026-04-06
sources: []
tags: [overview, observations]
confidence: subjective
---

- I definitely have Bipolar
- Cauda equina like symptoms come and go (its very odd)
- As of April 2026, on a stable dose of electrolytes and salt (2x bags of Dioralyte a day and +6 grams of salt a day in 600ml of water), fatigue symptoms seem to have become worse, not stable. In the UK 2x Liquid IV daily seemed to work better than Dioralyte. 
- Two major dystonia/parkinsonism/functional neurological motor symptom crisis - one in 2022 and another one in 2026. In 2022 I was on a combination of 300mg Seroquel SR or quetiapine and 50mg Lamictal. In 2026 I was on 600mg of lithium and had just tapered off quetiapine, which had been at 100mg or 50mg for years (since 2022). 
- Paresthesia is a recurring symptom. It happened in 2021 and returned in force in 2026. I had it very strongly alongside the first new motor symptom crisis in 2026. Then again when the cauda equina symptoms showed up. And they still remain to this day. 
- Loss of sensation in upper arms particularly in upper right arm is a common symptom. If I sleep on an arm, I might lose sensation on it for several minutes, which is pretty scary. I try to avoid this now.

# TC Crânio-Encefálica — 27-02-2018

**Data:** 27-02-2018
**Paciente:** Patient
**Médico requisitante:** Médico Referente A (Guimarães)
**Instituição:** Centro de Imagiologia A (Guimarães)
**Médico relator:** Radiologista A (Guimarães)

---

## Verbatim Transcription

**INFORMAÇÃO CLÍNICA:** "Doente com patologia do foro psíquico. Para exclusão de doença orgânica."

**TC CRÂNIO-ENCEFÁLICA**

**TÉCNICA:**
Orientados por topograma digital lateral, efectuaram-se cortes tomográficos axiais de 2,5mm de espessura para estudo da fossa posterior e de 5mm de espessura para avaliação do compartimento supra-tentorial.

**RELATÓRIO:**

O parênquima encefálico não apresenta alteração morfológica ou densitométrica, focal ou difusa.

Não é visível lesão endocraniana com localização intra ou extra-axial, nomeadamente de natureza expansiva.

Sistemas basais, ventrículos, espaços cisternais e sulcos corticais cerebrais com forma e dimensões normais. Ausência de colecções peri-contraste.

Sem sinais de conflito ao nível do buraco occipital.

Não se observa lesão óssea localizada na calote ou na base do crânio.

Correcta apresentação dos seios peri-nasais e das cavidades antro-timpânicas e das células mastoideas.

---

> **English translation note:**
> 
> **Clinical information:** "Patient with psychiatric pathology. To exclude organic disease."
> 
> **Brain CT scan**
> 
> **Technique:** Guided by digital lateral topogram, axial CT slices of 2.5mm thickness for posterior fossa study and 5mm thickness for supratentorial compartment evaluation.
> 
> **Report:** Brain parenchyma shows no morphological or densitometric alteration, focal or diffuse. No visible intracranial lesion, intra- or extra-axial, namely of expansive nature. Basal systems, ventricles, cisternal spaces and cortical cerebral sulci with normal shape and dimensions. No peri-contrast collections. No signs of conflict at the occipital foramen level. No bone lesion in the calvarium or skull base. Normal presentation of paranasal sinuses, anterior-tympanic cavities and mastoid cells.

# GP Letter — Psychiatrist A (London) — 08-03-2019

**Clinic Date:** 8 March 2019
**Paciente:** Patient
**Psychiatrist:** Psychiatrist A (London) — Consultant Psychiatrist
**Addressed to:** GP Surgery A (London)
**Type:** Initial assessment — GP letter

---

## Verbatim Transcription

8 March 2019

Clinic Date: 8 March 2019

Dear Doctor

Re: Mr Patient [SURNAME REMOVED] - dob [DOB REMOVED]
[ADDRESS REMOVED]

I had the pleasure to meet today during my outpatients clinic at [Clinic A (London)] Mr Patient [SURNAME REMOVED].

At the time of our first meeting, Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] was taking Abilify 10mg, mane and Promethazine 50mg, nocte for a manic relapse of his bipolar disorder.

Today he comes to the clinic as afflicted by restlessness and asking for alternatives to current medications.

Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] recalls an hypomanic relapse in January 2019 when he started feeling easily irritated by people around him who he would find incredibly slow and would trigger violent thoughts about beating them up or punish them for being so slow. He also experienced racing thoughts, fluctuations in his mood with sudden changes from elation to low mood, increased sexual libido and overspending.

He asked to be reviewed by the public sector by was denied any urgent appointment. He then attended A&E and was given Abilify 10mg, mane but this gave him restlessness and increased appetite and was unable to work and carry on his normal life feeling so restless. He was recently taken on by home treatment team but has been discharged following a three days trip to Cologne to meet a woman he fell in love with.

He feels that Abilify has helped him and he can manage sleep with the Promethazine but it seems that he requires additional medications to aid with sleep, the racing thoughts have slightly dissipated and the violent thoughts have reduced; however, mood continues to fluctuate rapidly and still feel hypersexual and with a tendency to overspending. He specifies the sex is promiscuous but protected with consensual female adult partners met through phone apps. He denies any grandiose beliefs of delusional nature or any other psychotic symptom.

He is currently followed up by mental health services in [Borough] and [GP B (London)] in primary care. He was told that he had an appointment with the community mental health team on 18/03 but realised that he could not wait because of rapid deterioration of mental state.

**Past Psychiatric History**

Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] recalls a first manic episode in Feb 2018 following sentimental involvement with a woman. He thought he could see 'love' and thought he needed to start a new religion, he stopped sleeping, thought he was becoming a genius, started becoming hyper-religious going to Buddhist centre every day and then felt a 'detonation' after which he could see 'love', he could sense 'vibrations' coming out of living beings. After a while he began feeling unsafe with pressured speech and racing thoughts and started flooding the woman he was in love with text messages until she eventually recoiled and blocked him. Denies any auditory hallucination, thought broadcasting or insertion at the time.

He then recalls reading the symptoms of psychosis on the internet and recognising some of the features. He went to the GP who gave him sertraline. This triggered a rapid cycling episode.

He was eventually rescued by his father who took him back to Portugal where he was admitted to hospital for over a month and treated with Abilify first and Olanzapine later (dose unclear) together with Sodium Valproate at a relative low dose, 200mg or 400 mg (dose unclear).

He later had to stop Sodium Valproate because made him to drowsy. He also had to stop Abilify after a month because of erectile dysfunction. He reports undergoing a period of depression when he spent a month in bed. He later started to recuperate going to the gym, he found a new job and slowly started feeling better. He continued Sodium Valproate 200mg, in divided doses until July 2018 and eventually stopped in August because he felt low and couldn't concentrate at work.

In January 2019, when he started experiencing the first manic symptoms he went to the GP and was given Sodium Valproate 200mg, in divided dose but had bad digestive problem with diarrhoea alternated to constipation, He asked for a referral to the public sector but was told that he could be seen only in two months. Then he went to A&E and hospitalised for one night and recommended to start Abilify 10 mg, mane and to stop Sodium valproate in view of the digestive collateral effects.

**Medical history**
Nil of note. No allergies.

**Family History**
Father and mother in their 60ies. Mother possibly affected by dementia.
Younger brother tried to commit suicide at 11 ys. old. Eldest brother suffered from a depressive episode.

**Past Psychiatric History**
Patient describes himself with a cyclothymic temperament. Saw a psychologist early on as had a difficult upbringing. Works as a video-editor in London. Lives in shared household. Has a good support network of friends aware of his bipolar illness.

**Drugs & Alcohol History**
Has taken recreational drugs like MDMA, hashish and marijuana in the past. Has not touched drugs in the past 6 months as aware of negative impact on his mental state. Has not used alcohol in the past 3-4 weeks for same reasons.

**Forensic History**
Nil of note.

**Mental State Examination**
Young and slim Caucasian male well groomed, slightly overfamiliar. Visibly agitated with increased psychomotor agitation, standing up and pacing around. Speech increased in rate. Mood easily changeable, irritable at times. His thoughts are not always congruent and goal directed and present with derailment and tangentiallity. Denies abnormality of perception or any current delusional beliefs. No current risks to self or others detected during this meeting. Only risk is of further deterioration if left untreated.

**Formulation**
Manic relapse in bipolar disorder. We discussed different treatment options in terms of antipsychotic and mood stabilisers medications. He has preferred Quetiapine after hearing side effects profile.

**Plan**
I recommended to start Quetiapine XL 300mg, tonight to be increased to 600mg, nocte starting tmw night and to meet soon next week Wednesday 13/03/19 at 20.00.

---



---

# GP Letter — Psychiatrist A (London) — 13-03-2019

**Clinic Date:** 13 March 2019
**Paciente:** Patient
**Psychiatrist:** Psychiatrist A (London) — Consultant Psychiatrist
**Addressed to:** GP Surgery A (London)
**Type:** Follow-up — GP letter

---

## Verbatim Transcription

13 March 2019

Clinic Date: 13 March 2019

Dear Doctor

Re: Mr Patient [SURNAME REMOVED] - dob [DOB REMOVED]
[ADDRESS REMOVED]

I had the pleasure to meet again Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] today for a follow up appointment during my outpatients' clinic at [Clinic A (London)].

Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] was taking Quetiapine XL 600mg, nocte for a manic relapse of a bipolar disorder as per clinic letter dated 08/03/19.

Today Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] reports great improvement of his mental state and states feeling fine and stable 'very normal'. He is able to sleep a lot better without the aid of Promethazine for 8 hours per night. Also his mood has greatly normalised without any feature of irritability and without harbouring violent thoughts for the less energetic and able ones. Sexual function and libido have also reduced to baseline and he is now able to function and concentrate at work, he does not experience racing thoughts any longer. He has recently gone back to work as free-lance and he is now teaching in Brighton for few days a week. He complains of milder fluctuations of his mood however these are much more bearable than previously. His current main fear is a depressive episode which he knows it normally follows mania.

Today Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] presents much more composed and appropriate with normal levels of engagement and normal speech. Significantly calmer with no psychomotor agitation or restlessness. Mood is rated subjectively as within his normal usual range and objectively noted as slightly subdued. No delusional beliefs or abnormalities of perception are reported and no indirect signs are detected. Cognition is normal with excellent insight into his mental health needs and the need to take medications. There are no risks to self or others detected during today's meeting.

We discussed the opportunity to start a mood stabiliser as this will need to be his long term treatment strategy since it is opportune to withdraw antipsychotic medication after 4 weeks from complete resolution of psychotic symptoms as per BAP and Maudsley Guidelines. This to reduce the risk of onset of depressive episodes. Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] expresses a preference for Lamictal as mood stabiliser for its benign side effect profile.

I recommended to continue taking Quetiapine XL 600mg, nocte for the time being and to start Lamictal 25 mg, mane for 14 days and to increment 25mg, every 14 days until it reaches 100mg, mane as per BNF titration.

I would be very grateful if you could start repeat prescription for Quetiapine XL 600mg, nocte and Lamictal 25mg, mane for 14 days and if you could continue to titrate Lamictal according to BNF-that is with an increment of 25 mg every 14 days until it reaches 100mg, mane.

Should you have any queries please do not hesitate to ask.

Yours sincerely

[Psychiatrist A (London)]
Consultant Psychiatrist

---

# GP Letter — Psychiatrist A (London) — 06-11-2019

---

## Verbatim Transcription

6 November 2019

Clinic Date: 6 November 2019

Dear Doctor

Re: Mr Patient [SURNAME REMOVED] - dob [DOB REMOVED]
[ADDRESS REMOVED]

I had the pleasure to meet again Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] today for a follow up appointment during my outpatients' clinic at [Clinic A (London)].

Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] is taking Quetiapine XL 300mg, nocte and Lamictal 150 mg, mane.

Patient comes back to the clinic asking for his medications to be changed to Seroquel and Lamictal instead of the generic brand. He states that he has been unstable since the last time we met in may and is unhappy about the public sector. He tells me that Seroquel was changed to immediate release and that formulation knocked him out and was unable to wake up the next day. He reports that mood has been unstable feeling more easily irritated, nervous, impatient or quick tempered. He also easily plunged into depression with poor motivation, depressed mood and frequent headaches.

He denies any angry outburst, any frank manic or psychotic symptoms.

Today he presents his usual pleasant and talking individual. His speech was normal for rate and volume. He has reactive affect and normal mood. No manic or psychotic symptoms were reported nor indirect signs were noted. He denies any thought/intention or plan to harm self or others.

We discussed how unlikely it may be that current variation in his mood and energy levels may due to the changes of the brand. I recommended him trying to transition on high dose of Lamotrigine/Lamictal or eventually trying Lithium if higher dose of Quetiapine were poorly tolerated.

For the time being her only asked for Seroquel and Lamictal to be prescribed and to evaluate at a later stage whether it was opportune to make any further change to his treatment plan.

I prescribed Patient with Seroquel XL 300mg, nocte (10 tabs) and Lamictal 150 mg, mane (10 tabs).

I would be grateful if you could continue repeat prescription for same meds: Seroquel XL 300mg, nocte and Lamictal 150 mg, mane.

Yours sincerely

[Psychiatrist A (London)]
Consultant Psychiatrist

# GP Letter — Psychiatrist A (London) — 18-09-2020

**Clinic Date:** 18 September 2020
**Letter Date:** 21 September 2020
**Paciente:** Patient
**Psychiatrist:** Psychiatrist A (London) — Consultant Psychiatrist
**Addressed to:** GP Surgery A (London)
**Type:** Follow-up (phone) — GP letter — **DISCHARGE from caseload**

---

## Verbatim Transcription

21 September 2020

Clinic Date: 18 September 2020

Dear Dr

Re: Mr Patient [SURNAME REMOVED] - dob [DOB REMOVED]
[ADDRESS REMOVED]

I had the pleasure to talk to Patient again today over the phone for a follow up appointment and as part of my outpatients' clinic at [Clinic A (London)].

At the time of our appointment Patient was taking Quetiapine XL 300mg, nocte and Lamictal at the variable dose of 250-300mg, mane. This with good effect.

He does report 6 months of well-being with overall stable mood, energy levels and functioning. He has been steady and consistent with his rhythms at work, and continues to be in a relationship with Brazilian woman that has now joined him to live together in Portugal. Describes his mood as stable and calm however has registered a bit of a drop in the month of June which has prompted him to reduce the dose of Lamictal from 300mg, mane to 250mg, mane and more recently in the month of August he reports experiencing a couple hours of high with increased speech and elated mood towards the end of the day each day. He recalls that taking Quetiapine XL 300mg, nocte did curb it down. This mood change prompted him to increase the Lamictal back again to 300mg, mane.

He believes is happy with current combination of mood. I have advised him to slightly increase Quetiapine of 50mg max 100mg, for a total of 400mg, nocte should he experience another episode of elation and leave the dose of Lamictal unchanged or engage in a slow and careful increase of Lamictal up to 400mg, OD (normally Lamictal tends to act more slowly than Quetiapine).

He reports having felt particularly low at the beg of this week but this is likely to be due to COVID infection which appears to be mild. He is experiencing some of the symptoms- fever, muscle aches and headaches – but only managed to get a test privately so unclear whether this is a COVID-related infection. He has been advised to self-isolate for 10 days which he will. He is aware of following steps should his condition deteriorate.

He is planning to go back to Portugal as he finds it more conducive to his recovery and stability also of his mental health and now that he can work remotely does not find any reason to be in London.

I was not able to complete a full assessment of his mental state over the phone; however, he sounded pleasant and engaging as usual. Reactive in affect and in good spirit with no delusional beliefs and no abnormalities of perception reported or detected. I did not detect any risk to self or others during today's conversation.

I congratulated Patient for the good work done and progress made. I believe that he is now in full recovery however he will need to continue current medications.

I confirmed current combination of medication at current dose and suggested for him to be followed up by a psychiatrist in his local area which he says he will.

I now discharge Patient from my caseload wishing him the very best for his future.

Yours sincerely

[Psychiatrist A (London)]
Consultant Psychiatrist

---

**TERAPÊUTICA PROPOSTA**

**RECOMENDAÇÕES APÓS ALTA**

As situações clínicas têm uma evolução natural e muitas vezes não é possível fazer o diagnóstico nas primeiras horas da doença. Assim, siga as recomendações que lhe foram transmitidas e caso o seu estado de saúde se agrave, deverá recorrer de novo aos nossos serviços.

Em caso de dúvida contacte-nos através do telefone ________________________

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> Male, 31 years old. Past history: Bipolar disorder — with great seasonal variability. Medications: Seroquel 300 mg extended-release at night; Lamictal 50 mg once daily morning; Aspirin (self-initiated). No known drug allergies.
>
> Moderate headache with associated dizziness and paraesthesias in the right upper limb for 4 days. Reports asthenia. Already seen in the ER and by neurology.
>
> Patient was seen 23/08/2021 by [Neurologist B (Porto)].
>
> Now with MRI results: "diagnosis of small neuroglial cyst in the topography of the right lingual gyrus with 6mm greatest axis… imaging follow-up suggested to exclude progressive character. At the left suboccipital level, planes posterior to the left occipital condyle, a rounded lesion with regular borders measuring approximately 1.6cm greatest dimensions in the axial plane of fibrotic character, may benefit from clarification by neck CT for differential diagnosis."
>
> Patient also reports DD of 480...
>
> **Examination:** Conscious, cooperative, oriented. Well-coloured and hydrated. Haemodynamically stable. Neurological exam normal.
>
> Contacted [Neurologist B (Porto)]: gives diazepam 5mg IV and schedules neurosurgery consultation.
>
> Refuses medication. States he wants a diagnosis. Extensive conversation with patient: explained that all tests have been done and he would benefit from medication to relieve his reported complaints...
>
> **Discharged against medical advice.**
>
> **Treatment given:** Diazepam 10mg/2ml injectable solution IM/IV — 5 mg
> **Discharge diagnosis:** 7840 - Headache



---

## Verbatim Transcription

DATA DE ADMISSÃO: 06-09-2021 HORA DE ADMISSÃO: 18:08
DATA DE ALTA CLÍNICA: 06/09/2021 HORA DE ALTA CLÍNICA: 23:04

ESTADO DO DOENTE: ____________________________________________

**RESUMO\ EVOLUÇÃO CLÍNICA**

Homem de 32 anos.
AP:
# Pert Bipolar - com grande variabilidade sazonal.
MH: seroquel 300 mg LP noite; lamictal 50 mg id manhã; AAS (por iniciativa própria).

Vem ao AP por dor torácica esquerda desde há semanas e agravado desde há 2-3 dias. Dor é tipo facada (SIC). Doente acha que pode ter miocardite devido a toma de vacina Covid ..

Sem dispneia ou palpitações.

Sem febre ou outras queixas.

Ansiedade.
CCO.
Corado e hidratado.
Apiretico.

ACP: N.

TA 120/67 mmHg, Fc 68 bpm.

Colhe analises, ECG, Rx torax.

PASSADO DO TURNO ANTERIOR, VER REGISTOS

Refere dor torácica há esq, que terá iniciado 2 dias apos toma da vacina. Teve várias avaliações netse contexto. Encontra-se a fazer doseamento semanal de d-dímeros (?)
Hoje com d-dímero ~600
Refere medo associado ao episódio. Mantém dor torácica à esq, que agrava com a inspiração
Melhoria apos toma de naproxeno.

Clínica de toráca, desde há semanas, apos toma de vacina.

Score Wells para TEP- 0 + d-dímero 600 --> baixa probabilidade
Varias observações neste contexto.
Peço Angio-TC

---

O mediastino apresenta-se na linha média exibindo normalidade morfodimensional. Normal permeabilidade e calibre das artérias pulmonares, sem sinais de TEP.
Não são individualizadas formações mediastino-hilares anómalas, nomeadamente de natureza adenomegálica.
A análise do parênquima pulmonar em janela densitométrica apropriada não demonstra alterações valorizáveis, nomeadamente não se observam infiltrados nem condensações parenquimatosas ou nodularidades tecidulares suspeitas de traduzir patologia evolutiva.
A árvore respiratória traqueobrônquica preserva normal calibre, sem evidência de bronquiectasias.
Ausência de derrame pericárdico ou pleural.

Medico sintomaticamernte
Explico sinais de alarme para nova avaliação médica
alta

**EXAMES AUXILIARES**

Ureia sérica [Urémia] ; Ionograma sérico; TC TORAX; Creatinaquinase Total (CK); RX TORAX, PULMOES E CORACAO 2 INCIDENCIAS; GPT / ALT [Alanina Aminotransferase]; GOT / AST [Aspartato Aminotransferase]; Mioglobina; ANGIO TAC; Proteína C Reactiva [PCR]; ECG SIMPLES; Dímeros-D de Fibrina (Doseamento); Creatinaquinase MB (Massa); Hemograma com plaquetas; Tempo de Protrombina (INR); Troponina I; Bilirrubinas (Total e Directa); Creatinina sérica [Creatininémia];

**DIAGNÓSTICOS DE SAÍDA**

Diagnósticos Secundários: 78650 - DOR TORACICA NAO ESPECIFICADA;

**TERAPÊUTICA PROPOSTA**

**RECOMENDAÇÕES APÓS ALTA**

As situações clínicas têm uma evolução natural e muitas vezes não é possível fazer o diagnóstico nas primeiras horas da doença. Assim, siga as recomendações que lhe foram transmitidas e caso o seu estado de saúde se agrave, deverá recorrer de novo aos nossos serviços.

Em caso de dúvida contacte-nos através do telefone ________________________

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> 32-year-old man. Past history: Bipolar disorder — with great seasonal variability. Medications: Seroquel 300 mg extended-release at night; Lamictal 50 mg once daily morning; Aspirin (self-initiated).
>
> Presents to ER with left chest pain for weeks, worsened over last 2-3 days. Pain is stabbing type (SIC). Patient thinks he may have myocarditis from Covid vaccine.
>
> No dyspnoea or palpitations. No urinary, respiratory or GI complaints. No fever. Good general condition. Anxiety. Conscious, cooperative, oriented. Well-coloured and hydrated. Afebrile. Cardiopulmonary auscultation: Normal. BP 120/67 mmHg, HR 68 bpm.
>
> Bloods, ECG, chest X-ray ordered.
>
> **Handover from previous shift:** Reports left chest pain started 2 days after vaccine. Multiple evaluations in this context. Weekly D-dimer monitoring (?). Today D-dimer ~600. Reports fear. Left chest pain persists, worse with inspiration. Improves with naproxen.
>
> Wells score for PE: 0 + D-dimer 600 → low probability. CT Angiography requested.
>
> **CT Angiography result:** Mediastinum midline with normal morphology. Normal patency and calibre of pulmonary arteries, **no signs of PE**. No abnormal mediastinal-hilar formations. Lung parenchyma shows no significant abnormalities — no infiltrates, consolidations, or suspicious nodules. Tracheobronchial tree normal calibre, no bronchiectasis. **No pericardial or pleural effusion.**
>
> Symptomatic treatment. Warning signs explained. Discharged.
>
> **Discharge diagnosis:** 78650 - Unspecified chest pain

# Angio TAC / TC Tórax — 06-09-2021

**Data Exame:** 06/09/2021
**Paciente:** Patient, 32 anos
**Instituição:** Hospital A (Porto)
**Radiologista:** Radiologista C (Porto)
**Exames:** ANGIO TAC (06-09-2021); TC TORAX (06-09-2021)

---

## Verbatim Transcription

**RELATÓRIO:**

**TOMOGRAFIA COMPUTORIZADA TORÁCICA**
(Urgência)

**INFORMAÇÃO CLÍNICA:**

" dor torácica à esq, desde háhá 2 semanas atrás, que iniciaram apos toma de vacina..."

**TÉCNICA:**

*Exame efetuado em equipamento multidetetor de 160 cortes e tecnologia de baixa dose de radiação.* Estudo efetuado pela técnica helicoidal multicorte, com aquisição volumétrica de imagens dos vértices pulmonares ao plano das glândulas suprarrenais, durante a injeção e.v. de contraste iodado não iónico.

**RELATÓRIO:**

O mediastino apresenta-se na linha média exibindo normalidade morfodimensional. Normal permeabilidade e calibre das artérias pulmonares, sem sinais de TEP.

Não são individualizadas formações mediastino-hilares anómalas, nomeadamente de natureza adenomegálica.

A análise do parênquima pulmonar em janela densitométrica apropriada não demonstra alterações valorizáveis, nomeadamente não se observam infiltrados nem condensações parenquimatosas ou nodularidades tecidulares suspeitas de traduzir patologia evolutiva.

A árvore respiratória traqueobrônquica preserva normal calibre, sem evidência de bronquiectasias.

Ausência de derrame pericárdico ou pleural.

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> **Chest CT Angiography** (Emergency)
>
> **Clinical information:** "Left chest pain for about 2 weeks, which started after taking the vaccine..."
>
> **Technique:** 160-slice multidetector equipment with low-dose radiation. Helical multislice technique, volumetric acquisition from lung apices to adrenal glands, during IV non-ionic iodinated contrast injection.
>
> **Report:**
> - Mediastinum midline with normal morphology and dimensions
> - **Normal patency and calibre of pulmonary arteries, no signs of PE (pulmonary embolism)**
> - No abnormal mediastinal-hilar formations, namely no lymphadenopathy
> - Lung parenchyma shows no significant abnormalities — no infiltrates, consolidations, or suspicious tissue nodules
> - Tracheobronchial tree normal calibre, no bronchiectasis
> - **No pericardial or pleural effusion**
>
> **Conclusion: Normal chest CT angiography. No PE, no myocarditis signs on CT.**

Não tem características [susp]eitas, não marca de forma [anómala] após contraste, nem apresenta restrição à difusão da [molécula] do gás. O estudo [complementar]mente com espectroscopia revela [curva] espectral [comp]atível com parênquima [cerebral] normal, tendo sido colocado [voxel] de interresse na [transitória] [cortical] [adjecent]e à [lesão]. Também não [é evidenciável] sinais [de hipoperfusão] no território da artéria basilar [ou da artéria] [vertebral].

Existem [hemorragias] [residuais] [ao redor] [de] [algumas] [estruturas hematológicas] [periventriculares].

Ao nível [da articulação] [cra]nio [se] verificava [a] [anterioridade] [referida] [ao côndilo] [esq].

Amígdalas cerebelosas em topografia adequada.

Sem [persistência] [de] topografia adequada.

Cervical sem [anormalidades]. Sem desenvolvimento significativo de disco [cervical] nas [estruturas verte]brais. # TC Pescoço — 14-09-2021

**Data Exame:** 14/09/2021
**Paciente:** Patient, 32 anos
**Instituição:** Hospital A (Porto)
**Radiologista:** Radiologista B (Porto)

---

## Verbatim Transcription

**RELATÓRIO:**

**TOMOGRAFIA COMPUTORIZADA DO PESCOÇO**

**TÉCNICA:**

*Exame efetuado em equipamento multidetetor de 160 cortes e tecnologia de baixa dose de radiação.* Realizada aquisição volumétrica desde a base do crânio até ao plano dos vértices pulmonares, antes e após a administração de contraste iodado por via endovenosa.

**RELATÓRIO:**

As imagens obtidas documentam regularidade do revestimento mucoso faringolaríngeo, não sendo aparentes lesões mucosas, com características de suspeição e tradução tomodensitométrica.

Cordas vocais simétricas, com normal morfologia.

Seios piriformes e valéculas livres.

Não são apreciáveis significativas alterações dos seios perinasais.

A avaliação das cadeias linfáticas laterocervicais não demonstra adenomegalias, bilateralmente.

Faz-se referência a formação nodular adjacente ao côndilo occipital esquerdo, com cerca de 16x14mm, de morfologia ovalar, com captação hipervascular após administração de contraste iodado, traduzindo aparente malformação vascular, questionando-se no contexto de aneurisma de V3 da artéria vertebral esquerda, aspeto que poderá ser confirmado por estudo angiográfico, caso clinicamente indicado.

Refere-se discreta vascularização colateral, locorregional, não sendo no entanto aparentes outras significativas alterações vasculares, com tradução no presente estudo e com o protocolo utilizado.

Regista-se simetria estrutural das glândulas salivares que preservam normal morfologia e densidade.

Não são apreciáveis significativas alterações da glândula tiroide.

Os vértices pulmonares intersetados não demonstram significativas alterações do parênquima pulmonar.

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> **CT Scan of the Neck**
>
> **Technique:** Performed on 160-slice multidetector equipment with low-dose radiation technology. Volumetric acquisition from skull base to lung apices, before and after IV iodinated contrast.
>
> **Report:**
> - Normal pharyngolaryngeal mucosal lining, no suspicious mucosal lesions
> - Symmetric vocal cords with normal morphology
> - Pyriform sinuses and valleculae clear
> - No significant paranasal sinus abnormalities
> - No laterocervical lymphadenopathy bilaterally
> - **Nodular formation adjacent to the left occipital condyle, approximately 16x14mm, oval, with hypervascular enhancement after contrast, representing apparent vascular malformation — possible V3 aneurysm of the left vertebral artery, which could be confirmed by angiographic study if clinically indicated**
> - Discrete collateral vascularisation noted locoregionally; no other significant vascular abnormalities
> - Salivary glands symmetric with normal morphology and density
> - No significant thyroid abnormalities
> - Lung apices show no significant parenchymal abnormalities



---

**Biomarcadores Cardíacos**

| Análises | Resultados | | Valores de Referência |
|---|---|---|---|
| Mioglobina Sérica | 12.0 | ng/ml | 10.0 - 46.0 |
| Troponina I cardíaca (cTn I - hs) | < 2 | ng/l | < 19 |

Interpretação:
Se Troponina I (hs) T0 > 100 ng/L, o utente deverá ser encaminhado para unidade de urgência hospitalar.

Utilizando o algoritmo para EAM sem elevação ST, baseado nos valores de Troponina I (hs) na admissão (T0) e a alteração no valor absoluto nas primeiras 2 horas (T2):

- Se Troponina I (hs) T0 < 2 ng/L ou se Troponina I (hs) T0 e T2 < 6 ng/L
(VPN* para EAM sem elevação ST: 99.4%)
- Se Troponina I (hs) T0 >= 100 ng/L ou se Troponina I (hs) T2-T0 >= 10 ng/L
(VPP** para EAM sem elevação ST: 74.5%)

Este algoritmo deve ter em conta o contexto clínico.
*VPN: Valor Preditivo Negativo
**VPP: Valor Preditivo Positivo

In: An algorithm for rule-in and rule-out of acute myocardial infraction using a

### Equilíbrio Hidroelectrolítico

**Ionograma sérico**
(Potenciometria Indirecta)

| Análises | Resultados | | Valores de Referência |
|---|---|---|---|
| Natrémia | 144.0 | mmol/l | 136.0 - 145.0 |
| Kaliémia | 4.1 | mmol/l | 3.5 - 5.1 |
| Clorémia | 103.0 | mmol/l | 98.0 - 107.0 |

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> Full blood panel from emergency visit on 06-09-2021 (chest pain post-Covid vaccine). Notable findings:
> - **D-Dimer mildly elevated** at 599.66 ng/ml (ref < 500) — context: weekly D-dimer monitoring post-vaccine
> - **CRP normal** at 0.070 mg/dL
> - **Troponin I normal** at < 2 ng/l (ref < 19) — rules out acute myocardial injury
> - All other values within normal range: CBC, coagulation, renal function, liver function, bilirubin, cardiac biomarkers, electrolytes
> - Platelets at low end of normal (157)

# GP Letter — Psychiatrist A (London) — 10-09-2021

**Clinic Date:** 10 September 2021
**Paciente:** Patient
**Psychiatrist:** Psychiatrist A (London) — Consultant Psychiatrist
**Type:** Follow-up (FaceTime) — GP letter — **DISCHARGE from care**

---

## Verbatim Transcription

10 September 2021

Clinic Date: 10 September 2021

Re: Mr Patient [SURNAME REMOVED] - dob [DOB REMOVED]
[ADDRESS REMOVED]

I had the pleasure to talk to Patient again today over FaceTime for a follow up appointment as part of my outpatients' clinic.

Patient is taking Quetiapine XL 300mg, nocte and stopped Lamictal.

Patient tells me that he had very bad side effects from vaccination on 16 August. He talks about neurological side effects such as lack of sensitivity on one side of the body, unable to move an arm and fatigue and brain fog. He completed all the necessary examination including CT scan and di-dimer which were all negative except for di-dimer whish was slightly raised (not clinically significant though).

He also tells me that he has stopped the Lamictal as felt too fatigued and low- he was unable to leave his bed until 2/3 o'clock in the afternoon. This was done with the authorisation of a psychiatrist in Portugal where he is currently residing. Since he stopped the Lamictal he continues to be fatigued but has problems with his sleep. He does not feel is reaching a manic or hypomanic phase.

He now feels a bit better that the side effects from vaccine are abating.

He presented well –casually dressed, pleasant and smiling. No signs of mania or symptoms reported. No risks detected during today's appointment.

My suggestions have been for him to increase Quetiapine XL to 400mg, nocte to resolve the difficulties with his sleep and restart Lamotrigine 25mg, mane for 14 days to be increased to 50mg, mane – this in order to avoid a manic relapse.

He will discuss suggestions given with his psychiatrist in Portugal.

I now discharge Patient from my care wishing him all the best for a prompt recovery.

Yours sincerely

[Psychiatrist A (London)]
Consultant Psychiatrist

---

- Sem edema assimetrico dos membros inferiores
- Equimose do pe direito em relação com os antecedentes descritos
- Pulso pedioso palpavel; Fluxometria trifasica ATA e ATP D

aPTT-Tempo Parcial de Tromboplastina activada; Ureia sérica [Urémia]; Ionograma sérico; Creatinaquinase Total (CK); ANGIO TAC; Mioglobina; Desidrogenase Láctica-LDH (Soro); GPT / ALT [Alanina Aminotransferase]; GOT / AST [Aspartato Aminotransferase]; Proteína C Reactiva [PCR]; ECG SIMPLES; Creatinaquinase MB (Massa); Dímeros-D de Fibrina (Doseamento); Troponina I; Hemograma com plaquetas; Tempo de Protrombina (INR); Bilirrubinas (Total e Directa); Creatinina sérica [Creatininémia];

Em caso de dúvida contacte-nos através do telefone ________________________

> **English translation note:**
>
> 32-year-old man. Past history: Bipolar disease. Distal diaphysis fracture of M5 (5th metatarsal), without significant displacement on 6/11/2021. On Lovenox (enoxaparin) 40 mg/day. Medications: Seroquel.
>
> Presents with sensation of fainting with anterior chest pressure about 3 hours ago. Denies chest pain, palpitations or dyspnoea. Also reports hypoaesthesia of right foot toes since splint was placed. Requests orthopaedic evaluation.
>
> Good general condition. Marked anxiety. Cardiopulmonary auscultation: no apparent abnormalities. Plaster splint on right foot.
>
> **ECG:** Sinus rhythm, HR 78 bpm, no signs of acute ischaemia. **Myocardial necrosis markers:** negative.
>
> **D-dimers elevated** → CT Angiography ordered: **No signs of acute PE** up to segmental level. Normal cardiovascular pedicle. Pre-vascular space densification related to thymic remnant/rebound. No pericardial or pleural effusion. No mediastinal/hilar lymphadenopathy. No parenchymal masses or consolidations. Non-specific 4mm peripheral nodular densification in the superior segment of the right lower lobe with smaller ones below. No cavitated lesions, pneumothorax, or interstitial changes.
>
> **Orthopaedics:** Bruising on dorsum of foot and calf pain. Suggests walker boot. No further orthopaedic care needed currently.
>
> **Vascular Surgery:** EcoDoppler — **no images suggestive of superficial or deep vein thrombosis** in right lower limb. No clinical or imaging evidence of DVT or SVT. Should maintain thromboembolism prophylaxis.
>
> **Discharge diagnosis:** 7802 - Syncope and collapse

### Patologia Química

**Enzimologia**

**Biomarcadores Cardíacos**

| Análises | Resultados | | Valores de Referência | Anteriores 08-11-2021 | Anteriores 06-09-2021 |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|

Interpretação:
Se Troponina I (hs) T0 > 100 ng/L, o utente deverá ser encaminhado para unidade de urgência hospitalar.

Utilizando o algoritmo para EAM sem elevação ST, baseado nos valores de Troponina I (hs) na admissão (T0) e a alteração no valor absoluto nas primeiras 2 horas (T2):

- Se Troponina I (hs) T0 < 2 ng/L ou se Troponina I (hs) T0 e T2 < 6 ng/L

> - CK-MB normal at 1.50 ng/ml
> - **Troponin I still normal** at < 2 ng/l — serial testing confirms no acute myocardial injury
> - Myoglobin normal at 29.0 ng/ml

## FILE: Transcripts Anonymous/2021/Reference/I-RECOVER-Protocol-Personal-Account-2021.md

---
title: I-RECOVER Protocol Personal Account
type: timeline
created: 2021-01-01
updated: 2026-04-06
sources: []
tags: [treatment, covid, protocol]
confidence: subjective
---

# Personal Account — I-RECOVER Protocol and Mast Cell Activation (2021)

**Type:** Personal blog/forum post (saved as PDF)
**Author:** Patient (self-authored)
**Context:** Post-Janssen vaccine adverse effects experience

---

## Verbatim Transcription

YSK about the I-RECOVER protocol from the FLCCC and Mast Cell Activation - my side effects seem improve after I had some over the counter anti histamines and regular supplements that are indicated for long haul covid

Hey fellas,
I've been posting for a while just wanted to share my experience. 32M, had 1 month of serious symptoms, mostly cleared up with anti histamines and supplement diet. Johnson vacc.

**TLDR - there's a list at the end with my supplement diet.**

Symptoms
Day 1-3 normal headaches, went away. By the end of day 3 I felt ready to come back to work.
BUT THEN
Day 4 came up. No feeling on the entire right side of my body. Hospital, CT scan. All clean. Slowly recover.
Day 5 came up. I can't lift my right arm and feel enormous weakness on right leg. Hospital, CT Scan again! I get muscle spams throughout my body and I think I'm going to be really poorly. BUT Still all clean. Blood tests. Fine. What do I do ? They give me diazepam. "It's psychological". Bullcrap, but in my southern european country there is no medical protocol to help with vaccine side effects… I learn this after 5 to 6 hospital visits, for multiple different things after the vaccine. I keep thinking I might be having clotting because of this constant leg pain, so I take aspirin 100mg to thin the blood. When I learn about D-dimer tests, they are indeed high but only slightly. "Not at risk" they tell me.

What follows is a month of hell. Tremors in my hands, difficulty walking. Always weakness in the right side of my body. Headaches for 2 weeks. Can't work. I get these "flashes of lightning" on my nerves that cause immense pain when they happen. Alcohol seems to make it worse.

Eventually I find two things

The I-RECOVER protocol by the Front Line covid 19 care alliance

And this medium post on how to deal with Mast Cell Activation and derived serotonin dysfunction

Now I get the stuff from the medium post first. Seems to help, but slowly. My supplement diet is the one they suggest:

Nicotinic acid aka Niacin (most important and not nicotinamide or other forms) — 100mg
Vitamin C aka Ascorbic Acid — 1500mg
Vitamin D — 3000iu
Zinc — 15mg
Selenium — 50mcg
Quercetin — 500mg

I skip the Zinc and Selenium at first since my Vitamin D seems to come with it. I later re-add them since I actually think that my initial supplements were *weak*.

I think this is pretty essential - find a good brand and get everything from them. I was getting some white label Vitamin D that SAID it had Zinc and Selenium, but looking back it was cheapo stuff and probably didn't really work, as their effect was limited to none.

The Quercetin I initially have no idea what it is, so I don't get it. **Big mistake!**
As when I find the I-RECOVER protocol, and take the time to really read it, Quercetin is listed there also as a Mast Cell Stabilizer!

From the I-RECOVER protocol, I start realising (3 weeks in!) that some of the medication listed in it are plain anti histamines, sold over the counter! In fact I have some cetirizine at home!

**Week 3 I take cetirizine immediately and I am HUGELY RELIEVED of symptoms.** Pins and needles are gone, I stop having weird feelings around my arm, feeling like my hands weren't quite grabbing things the way they used to.

I'm blown away. What the hell is going on? I then read that histamines are both part of the immune system, and neurotransmitters! Neurotransmitters? And I'm having unexplainable neurological symptoms?

**Ok, I'm all in on the Mast Cell Activation Syndrome theory now. I read up on everything that's in the I-RECOVER protocol.**

And I find that the following medication is available in my country over the counter:

Type 1 Histamines - Cetrizine 10mg
Type 2 Histamines - Famotidine 20mg

Mast Cell Stabilizers - Rupatadine 10mg

Word to the wise - **the dosages listed on the FLCCC list appear excessive to me.** When I read up on the effect of excess anti histamines, it includes heart issues, so I'm careful and I never took the Famotidine. I only took the Cetrizine and Rupatidine once in the same day, and even then had weird heart palpitations. And I always did it within the allowed dosages - 10 mg, and never tripled down as it says on the I-RECOVER protocol. **The FLCCC has been accused of overdosing and I must agree, I believe their dosages are way too high unless you have medical supervision.**

**So here's my advice - take Cetrizine to see if your symptoms alleviate.**

If they do, **DO NOT MIX unless you feel it's absolutely safe and necessary. My impression is the type 1 and type 2 histamines are just symptom relief anyway.** Really you want to find the Rupatadine (or its replacement on the list, Ketotifen). And in my opinion, if **Cetrizine seems to relieve your symptoms a lot, take the Rupatadine only!** That should be the medicine you need to relieve your Mast Cell Activation, if that is what you have.

Since Cetrizine worked so well, I looked at the supplements recommended within the I-RECOVER Protocol and bought them all.

Here's my final supplement diet

- Vitamin C — 500mg twice daily
- Omega-3 Fatty Acids — 4gm/daily (Vascepa, Lovaza, or DHA/EPA)
- ~~Melatonin — 2–10mg nightly, start with low dose, increase as tolerated in absence of sleep disturbance.~~ I don't do this as I already have sleep trouble.
- Vitamin D3 — 2,000–4,000 IU daily
- Quercetin — 500mg
- NAC (N-acetyl Cisteine) 600mg
- L-Glutathione 50mg
- Zinc — 15mg - *included in my VitC*
- Selenium — 50mcg - *included in my VitC*

I add
- Cetirizine 10mg if I have symptoms, for symptom relief (ie like painkiller).
- Rupatadine 10mg, *but only when I have had no cetirizine that day to avoid heart issues*.

**Also started doing a low histamine diet and avoiding alcohol ENTIRELY, which is a pain.** However alcohol and histamine high foods definitely make it worse. In fact alcohol seems to be the #1 cause for any relapses, and even having half a beer this weekend caused some issues.

For a few days I also did take paracetamol, which seemed to help, before I got on with the cetirizine. However I was told by a doctor not to take it for too long (more than a couple of days) as it's hard on your liver.

My impression - the change after I started taking cetrizine was amazing. I had some STRONG pins and needles, like my nervous system was "rebooting", the first couple of days. After that, my motor, pain and sensitivity issues went away. I am now 1 month and 2 days in and mostly recovered.

**Unresolved - Curiously I have bipolar disorder and used to take medication in the morning (Lamictal) to avoid me becoming manic during the day. Now, I don't have to take it. Most likely if I didn't have bipolar I would've been in a depressive state.** This is for now unresolved but I'm wondering about getting my psychiatrist to get me Fluvoxamine, which is the recommended anti depressive by the FLCCC. So I might try that eventually and report back later. However right now I am actually taking less medication than before, so this is a bonus for me, while it might be that some folks get deep depression after the shot.

I hope this helps someone else.

---



---

---

# Registo Poligráfico do Sono Noturno — 20-01-2022

**Data Exame:** 20 de Janeiro de 2022 (23h32min — 08h20min)
**Paciente:** Patient, 32 anos, IMC: 29.7 Kg/m²
**Instituição:** Hospital A (Porto)
**Médico requisitante:** [Pneumologista A (Porto)]
**Médica relatora:** [Especialista Medicina do Sono A (Porto)]

---

## Verbatim Transcription

**Registo Poligráfico do Sono Noturno**

Exame efetuado no dia 20 de Janeiro de 2022 cuja análise respeita ao período de tempo decorrido entre as 23h32min e as 08h20min.

*Registo Poligráfico do Sono Noturno, incluindo os seguintes parâmetros:*

Eletroencefalograma (6 canais), Eletro-oculograma (2 canais), Eletromiograma mentoniano (1 canal), Respiração torácica (1 canal), Respiração abdominal (1 canal), Fluxo nasal (1 canal), Fluxo oro-nasal (1 canal), Sensor de roncopatia (1 canal), Eletrocardiograma (1 canal), Eletromiograma tibial anterior bilateral (2 canais), Sensor de posição (1 canal) e Saturação de O₂.

---

**Análise da estrutura do sono**

O tempo total de sono foi de 8 horas e 33 minutos, sendo a eficiência de sono de 97.1%, encontrando-se dentro da normalidade.

A latência do sono é de 2.1 minutos, encontrando-se diminuída.

A percentagem de sono lento profundo e de sono paradoxal (REM) encontram-se diminuídas.

A ciclicidade do sono apresenta-se dentro da normalidade, tendo-se verificado fragmentação do sono.

---

**Análise dos parâmetros respiratórios/cardíacos**

Roncopatia ligeira, ocorrendo em 17.0% da noite.

Índice de Apneia/Hipopneia (IAH) = 7/h, tendo-se registado 3 apneias obstrutivas, 2 apneias centrais, 0 apneias mistas e 55 hipopneias, preferencialmente em sono paradoxal e sem fator posicional.

Valor mínimo de SaO₂ = 89.0%. Valor médio de SaO₂ = 94.0%.

Índice de dessaturação de oxigénio (IDO) = 2/h.

O parâmetro eletrocardiográfico, registado durante a noite, esteve de acordo com a normal variabilidade fisiológica ao longo do sono.

---

**Análise dos parâmetros eletromiográficos**

Não se registaram movimentos periódicos dos membros durante o sono de índice significativo.

---

**Conclusão**

Roncopatia e apneia obstrutiva do sono de índices ligeiros (IAH = 7/h), preferencialmente em sono paradoxal, sem dessaturações significativas de O₂ ao longo da noite.

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> **Nocturnal Sleep Polygraphy**
>
> **Sleep structure:** Total sleep time 8h33m, sleep efficiency 97.1% (normal). Sleep latency 2.1 minutes (decreased). Deep slow-wave sleep and REM sleep percentages are decreased. Sleep cyclicity normal but sleep fragmentation noted.
>
> **Respiratory/cardiac:** Mild snoring (17% of night). **AHI = 7/h** (3 obstructive apnoeas, 2 central apnoeas, 0 mixed, 55 hypopnoeas), predominantly in REM sleep, no positional factor. Min SpO₂ = 89%, Mean SpO₂ = 94%. ODI = 2/h. ECG normal variability.
>
> **EMG:** No significant periodic limb movements during sleep.
>
> **Conclusion: Mild snoring and mild obstructive sleep apnoea (AHI = 7/h), predominantly in REM, without significant O₂ desaturations.**



---

title: GP Letter — Psychiatrist A 2022-04-01
type: summary
created: 2022-04-01

# GP Letter — Psychiatrist A (London) — 01-04-2022

**Clinic Date:** 1 April 2022
**Letter Date:** 2 April 2022
**Paciente:** Patient
**Psychiatrist:** Psychiatrist A (London) — Consultant Psychiatrist, Honorary Senior Lecturer at UCL
**Addressed to:** GP Surgery A (London)
**Type:** Follow-up (Skype) — GP letter — **FINAL DISCHARGE from caseload**

---

## Verbatim Transcription

2 April 2022

Clinic Date: 1 April 2022

Dear Dr

Re: Mr Patient [SURNAME REMOVED] - dob [DOB REMOVED]
[ADDRESS REMOVED]

I had the pleasure to meet Patient today for a follow up appointment as part of my outpatients' clinic at [Clinic A (London)]. The consultation was held on Skype.

Patient is current taking Seroquel 300mg, nocte and Lamictal 50mg, mane.

He tells me that his life and mood are very stable. He continues to live in Porto where he work in postproduction for the film industry. At the time of the call he was attending a short course on screenwriting at well renowned film school outside of London. He met a new partner in Porto and does not think that he will relocate to London any time soon. He is facilitated by his job that can be done remotely.

However, he also tells me that he is getting concerned about his physical health. During Christmas he attended A&E for an episode of hyperglycaemia. He does admit that he ate too many sweets but does not think that it was excessive.

He completed HbA1c which he was told is bordering pre-diabetic levels. He also eliminated all the carbs and sugars in his diet and engaged in regular physical exercise but the glucose levels remain high. He believes that Seroquel may have contributed to glucose dysregulation.

Today [SURNAME REMOVED] presented very well, always jovial and intelligent. Smiling and bright with normal speech, coherent thinking and no manic or psychotic symptoms reported and none elicited. Cognition was intact. His insight is always very good and I did not detect any risk during today's consultation.

I did confirm that Seroquel can have an impact on metabolism and metabolic measure. It is rare but possible.

I recommended to complete a screening for diabetic and pre-diabetic condition and be supported by a specialist where he lives.

He also needs to consider, in conjunction with his psychiatrist and endocrinologist, whether to change current treatment plan. This will need to be carefully considered and weighted against risks of developing a frank diabetic condition and/ or a relapse of primary mental health condition, namely bipolar disorder.

I have known Patient for few years and he has in fact benefitted greatly from current treatment plan. Initially the idea was to transition to taking solely Lamictal but he never found comfortable in reducing Seroquel too much.

If it is considered necessary to change current treatment plan I would suggest the following options in the following order:

1) Cross-titrate current regime to Lamotrigine only at high dose -up to 400mg, daily as per BNF. Lamotrigine is an excellent mood stabiliser with no impact on metabolism or weight;
2) Alternatively, Patient can try a combination of Lamictal and Aripiprazole. I know that Patient tried Aripiprazole before without liking it too much but it was for a short period. I would encourage him to trial aripiprazole for a longer period before ruling it out. Please bear in mind that aripiprazole can also work as monotherapy.
3) If aripiprazole in combination or as monotherapy does not work, I would suggest trying Sodium Valproate in monotherapy or in combination with Lamictal. Sodium valproate is an excellent mood stabiliser. It may have an impact on metabolism and weight as well but less than quetiapine.
4) If all the above fails, I would suggest trying Lithium who is the gold standard for the treatment of bipolar disorder however comes with negative impact on kidney and thyroid in the longer term.

I told Patient that I was not able to provide him with support needed for this type of task and he needs an higher level of input than what can be given remotely as he would require frequent follow ups and also an understanding of the services available in his local area. I recommended Patient to find a psychiatrist he trusts in Porto that can support him whilst building together a treatment plan that Patient finds suitable without negative side effect on his physical health.

I now discharge him from my caseload wishing him the very best for his future.

Yours sincerely

[Psychiatrist A (London)]
Consultant Psychiatrist Honorary Senior Lecturer at UCL

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> 32-year-old male. Past history: bipolar disease. No surgical history. Medications: Seroquel, Lamictal. Non-smoker. No known drug allergies.
>
> **Presenting complaint:** Abdominal pain in the flank and left hypochondrium, intermittent, colicky, with sensation of distended abdomen. No bowel changes, no urinary complaints, no other associated symptoms.
>

Abdomen soft and depressible, painful on deep palpation of flank and left iliac fossa with associated tympanism, no signs of peritoneal irritation. Meningeal signs negative.
>
> Bloods and biochemistry: no abnormalities. Urinalysis: no abnormalities.
>
> **Abdominal ultrasound (emergency):** Liver normal size, regular contour, relatively homogeneous echostructure, no nodules or biliary duct dilation. Gallbladder minimally distended, no apparent intraluminal calculi or wall thickening. Pancreas and spleen show no relevant abnormalities, nor do kidneys. No lymphadenopathy or free/collected intraperitoneal fluid.
>
> **Conclusion:** Upper abdominal ultrasound without significant abnormalities, specifically in the context of left flank and hypochondrium pain.
>
> Discharged with medication; warning signs explained.
>
> **Discharge diagnosis:** 78900 - Abdominal pain, unspecified location
