# Ecografia Abdominal (Urgência) — 10-05-2022

**Data Exame:** 10/05/2022
**Paciente:** Patient, 32 anos
**Instituição:** Hospital A (Porto)
**Radiologista:** Radiologista H (Porto)

---

## Verbatim Transcription

**RELATÓRIO:**

**ECOGRAFIA ABDOMINAL (URGÊNCIA)**

O fígado apresenta dimensões normais, contorno regular e ecoestrutura relativamente homogénea, sem evidência de nódulos ou dilatação das vias biliares.

A vesícula, pouco distendida, não revela aparentes cálculos endoluminais nem espessamento parietal.

O pâncreas e o baço não sugerem alterações relevantes, assim como os rins, avaliados complementarmente de forma sumária.

Não se regista adenomegalias, nem líquido intraperitoneal livre ou coletado.

**CONCLUSÃO:**

Estudo ecográfico abdominal superior sem alterações valorizáveis, designadamente no alegado contexto de dor no flanco e hipocôndrio, à esquerda.

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> **Abdominal Ultrasound (Emergency)**
>
> - Liver: normal size, regular contour, relatively homogeneous echostructure, no nodules or biliary duct dilation
> - Gallbladder: minimally distended, no apparent intraluminal calculi or wall thickening
> - Pancreas and spleen: no relevant abnormalities; kidneys assessed briefly, also unremarkable
> - No lymphadenopathy or free/collected intraperitoneal fluid
>
> **Conclusion: Normal upper abdominal ultrasound, specifically in the context of left flank and hypochondrium pain.**

# Resultados Patologia Clínica — 01-05-2022 (Marcadores Cardíacos)

**Data de Inscrição:** 01-05-2022
**Data de Relatório:** 01-05-2022
**Paciente:** Patient, 32 A
**Instituição:** Hospital A (Porto) / Laboratório A
**Médico requisitante:** Médico Urgencista G (Porto)
**Patologista:** Patologista A

---

## Verbatim Transcription

### Patologia Química

**Biomarcadores Cardíacos**

| Análises | Resultados | | Valores de Referência |
|---|---|---|---|
| Mioglobina Sérica | 20.0 | ng/ml | 10.0 - 46.0 |
| Troponina I cardíaca (cTn I - hs) | < 2 | ng/l | < 19 |

(Ensaio Imunoenzimático)

Interpretação:
Se Troponina I (hs) T0 > 100 ng/L, o utente deverá ser encaminhado para unidade de urgência hospitalar.

Utilizando o algoritmo para EAM sem elevação ST, baseado nos valores de Troponina I (hs) na admissão (T0) e a alteração no valor absoluto nas primeiras 2 horas (T2):

- Se Troponina I (hs) T0 < 2 ng/L ou se Troponina I (hs) T0 e T2 < 6 ng/L
(VPN* para EAM sem elevação ST: 99.4%)
- Se Troponina I (hs) T0 >= 100 ng/L ou se Troponina I (hs) T2-T0 >= 10 ng/L
(VPP** para EAM sem elevação ST: 74.5%)

*VPN: Valor Preditivo Negativo
**VPP: Valor Preditivo Positivo

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> Cardiac markers from the 30-04/01-05-2022 chest pain ER visit. Both normal:
> - Myoglobin 20.0 ng/ml (ref 10-46) — normal
> - **Troponin I < 2 ng/l** (ref < 19) — rules out acute myocardial injury



---

# Relatório Anátomo-Patológico — 26-05-2022

**Data da colheita:** 26-05-2022
**Data de entrada:** 30-05-2022
**Data do relatório:** 31 de Maio de 2022
**Paciente:** Patient, 32A, Sexo M
**Instituição:** Laboratório B (Porto) — Laboratório de Patologia e Citopatologia
**Médico requisitante:** [Dermatologista A (Porto)] / Hospital A (Porto)
**Patologista relator:** [Patologista D (Porto)]

---

## Verbatim Transcription

**RELATÓRIO ANÁTOMO-PATOLÓGICO**

Natureza da peça: Pele

Informação Clínica: nevo melanocitico 1 cm na zona abdominal esquerda com irregularidade da rede

Material: Biópsia

Exame Requisitado: Histológico - biópsia incisional/excisional, raspagem, curetagem ou de eliminação espontânea

**Descrição Macroscópica:**

Retalho fusiforme de pele com 1,3x0,8x0,4cm, centrado por lesão ligeiramente elevada de superfície acastanhada e rugosa, e bordo irregular com 0,9x0,6cm, distando 0,1cm da margem mais próxima.

IT:4F2C-C1 e C2 (C1- topos; C2- lesão)

**Descrição Microscópica:**

Ao exame histológico observa-se nevo melânico com crescimento epidérmico e intradérmico.
Não se observam sinais de malignidade.
Margem de exérese sem lesão.

**Diagnóstico:**

Nevo melânico composto.

Topografia: T-0200 Morfologia: M-8760

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> **Anatomopathological Report — Skin Biopsy**
>
> **Clinical info:** 1cm melanocytic naevus in the left abdominal area with network irregularity.
>
> **Macroscopic:** Fusiform skin flap 1.3x0.8x0.4cm, centred by a slightly elevated lesion with brownish, rough surface and irregular border, 0.9x0.6cm, 0.1cm from nearest margin.
>
> **Microscopic:** Melanocytic naevus with epidermal and intradermal growth. **No signs of malignancy.** Excision margin clear of lesion.
>
> **Diagnosis: Compound melanocytic naevus.** (Benign)

# RM Crânio-Encefálica (Repetição) — 29-06-2022

**Data Exame:** 29/06/2022
**Paciente:** Patient, 32 anos
**Instituição:** Hospital A (Porto)
**Radiologista:** Radiologista E (Porto)

---

## Verbatim Transcription

**RELATÓRIO:**

**RESSONÂNCIA MAGNÉTICA CEREBRAL**

**INFORMAÇÃO CLÍNICA:**

"Lesão com hipersinal em TR longo com 8mm, sugestivo de lesão inespecífica/gliótica."

**TÉCNICA:**

*Exame efetuado em RM de alto campo (1.5 Tesla).* Obtiveram-se imagens axiais ponderadas em T1, DP, T2, T2* e difusão; cortes coronais T2. Aquisição volumétrica 3D/FLAIR.

**RELATÓRIO:**

Em comparação com o exame de 17.09.2021, permanece praticamente inalterado o hipersinal conhecido nas sequências de TR longo justacortical temporal mesial direito, envolvendo, possivelmente, o giro lingual direito, sem expansão associada e sem restrição à difusão das moléculas da água.

Não existem outras alterações valorizáveis do sinal ou da morfologia do parênquima encefálico.

Excluem-se hemorragias petequiais ou seguras coleções hemorrágicas pericerebrais.

As vias de circulação de líquor têm configuração e dimensões adequadas ao escalão etário.

Amígdalas cerebelosas em topografia adequada.

Espessamentos mucosos inflamatórios no pavimento dos seios maxilares.

Caixas timpânicas e mastoides com transparência conservada.

**CONCLUSÃO:**

Exame globalmente sobreponível ao realizado em 17.09.2021.

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> **Brain MRI (Follow-up)**
>
> **Clinical info:** "Lesion with high signal on long TR sequences measuring 8mm, suggestive of non-specific/gliotic lesion."
>
> **Technique:** 1.5 Tesla high-field MRI. Axial T1, PD, T2, T2* and diffusion; coronal T2; 3D/FLAIR volumetric acquisition.
>
> **Report:** Compared to the exam of 17.09.2021, the known high signal on long TR sequences in the right mesial temporal juxtacortical region remains **practically unchanged**, possibly involving the right lingual gyrus, without associated expansion and without restriction to water molecule diffusion.
>
> No other significant signal or morphological abnormalities of the brain parenchyma. No petechial haemorrhages or pericerebral haemorrhagic collections. CSF pathways with adequate configuration and dimensions for age. Cerebellar tonsils in adequate topography. Inflammatory mucosal thickening on the floor of the maxillary sinuses. Tympanic cavities and mastoids with preserved transparency.
>
> **Conclusion: Exam globally superimposable to the one performed on 17.09.2021.** (Stable known lesion, no progression.)



---

# TC Crânio — 29-08-2022

**Data Exame:** 29/08/2022
**Paciente:** Patient, 32 anos
**Instituição:** Hospital A (Porto)
**Radiologista:** Radiologista I (Porto)

---

## Verbatim Transcription

**RELATÓRIO:**

**TOMOGRAFIA COMPUTORIZADA CEREBRAL**

**TÉCNICA:**

Aquisição volumétrica multicorte (160 cortes) e tecnologia de baixa dose de radiação, com reconstruções axiais, coronais e sagitais de 3mm de espessura desde o plano do buraco magno até ao vértex, sem contraste.

**RELATÓRIO:**

Não encontramos lesões hemorrágicas endocranianas agudas.

Não se observam alterações da densidade do parênquima encefálico.

Exclui-se coleção pericerebral.

Sulcos da convexidade e sistema ventricular de configuração e amplitude normal.

Normalidade da charneira nervosa occipitovertebral.

Os seios perinasais abrangidos por este estudo, assim como os ouvidos médios, constituem cavidades globalmente transparentes.

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> **Brain CT Scan** (non-contrast)
>
> **Technique:** 160-slice volumetric multislice acquisition with low-dose radiation, axial/coronal/sagittal 3mm reconstructions from foramen magnum to vertex.
>
> **Report:**
> - **No acute intracranial haemorrhagic lesions**
> - No density abnormalities of brain parenchyma
> - No pericerebral collection
> - Convexity sulci and ventricular system normal configuration and amplitude
> - Normal occipitovertebral nervous junction
> - Paranasal sinuses and middle ears globally transparent
>
> **Conclusion: Normal brain CT.**

# Informação Clínica — Atendimento Permanente — 11-11-2022

**Data de Admissão:** 11-11-2022 **Hora de Admissão:** 11:14
**Data de Alta Clínica:** 11/11/2022 **Hora de Alta Clínica:** 14:55
**Paciente:** Patient, 33 anos
**Instituição:** Hospital A (Porto)
**Serviço:** Atendimento Permanente
**Médico responsável:** Médico Urgencista J (Porto)

---

## Verbatim Transcription

**Informação clínica - Atendimento Permanente**

**Resumo clínico do episódio:**

33 anos

Patologia Psiq- Dça Bipolar?
Sob Lamictal 50 + Seroquel 300

Vem por quadro de distonia e acatisia com 2 dias evolução
Doente filmou quadro no domicilio e que mantem
Sem alterações recentes da medicação

Observação em conjunto com [Neurologista B (Porto)]

Eo -sem defices sensitivo-motores face e membros
Presença de distonia.
Sem movimentos durante repouso

Analises - sem subida Ck. F renal N
ECG - sem perturbações ritmo/condução. QT-N

Fez Artane com ligeira melhoria

Refere recorrencia sintomas com doses mais baixas de Quetiapina

Inicia Artane e oriento para Psiquiatra Assistente - diz ter consulta a 15/11

**Exames realizados:**

Ureia sérica [Urémia]; Ionograma sérico; Creatinaquinase Total (CK); Glicémia em jejum; Mioglobina; Proteína C Reactiva [PCR]; ECG SIMPLES; Hemograma com plaquetas; Creatinina sérica [Creatininémia];

**Terapêutica realizada:**

MIDAZOLAM 15 MG/3 ML SOL INJ AMP IM/IV - 3 MG; TRI-HEXIFENIDILO 2 MG COMP OR - 2 MG;

**Diagnóstico:**

Diagnósticos Secundários: 33372 - DISTONIA AGUDA DEVIDA A FARMACOS;

**Sinais de Alerta/Recomendações:** As situações clínicas têm uma evolução natural e muitas vezes não é possível fazer o diagnóstico nas primeiras horas da doença. Assim, siga as recomendações que lhe foram transmitidas e caso o seu estado de saúde se agrave, deverá recorrer de novo a cuidados médicos.

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> 33 years old. Psychiatric pathology — Bipolar disease? On Lamictal 50 + Seroquel 300.
>
> **Presenting complaint:** Dystonia and akathisia for 2 days. Patient filmed the episode at home and it persists. No recent medication changes.
>
> **Examined jointly with [Neurologist B (Porto)].** No sensory-motor deficits of face and limbs. **Presence of dystonia.** No movements during rest.
>
> Bloods: no CK elevation. Renal function normal. ECG: no rhythm/conduction disturbances. QT normal.
>
> Given Artane (trihexyphenidyl) with slight improvement. Reports symptom recurrence with lower doses of Quetiapine.
>
> Starts Artane and referred to treating Psychiatrist — says he has appointment on 15/11.
>
> **Treatment given:** Midazolam 3mg IM/IV; Trihexyphenidyl 2mg oral.
> **Discharge diagnosis:** 33372 - **Acute dystonia due to drugs**



---

> - **24h urinary sodium very high** at 359 mEq/24h (ref 40-220) — significant natriuresis, consistent with renal concentrating defect / high salt intake (6g/day)
> - **24h urine volume:** 4350 ml — polyuria
> - **Plasma osmolality:** 280 mOsmol/Kg (normal, ref 275-295)
> - **Urine osmolality:** 287 mOsmol/Kg (low-normal for urine, ref 50-1400) — inappropriately dilute relative to polyuria, consistent with partial DI
> - **Sodium at upper limit** at 145.0 (ref 136-145)
> - **Platelets low** at 147 (ref 150-400) — persistent mild thrombocytopenia
> - **Lymphocytes slightly high** at 41.2% (ref 20-40)
> - **Lithium stable** at 0.42 (subtherapeutic, ref 0.60-1.20)
> - Ferritin normal at 84, CBC otherwise normal

# Prova de Esforço — 13-03-2026

**Data:** 13-03-2026
**Paciente:** Patient, 36 anos, Sexo M
**Instituição:** Hospital A (Porto)
**Médico requisitante:** [Cardiologista B (Porto)]
**Médico responsável pelo relatório:** [Cardiologista C (Porto)]
**Motivo:** Fadiga crónica; Disfunção autonómica


---

## Verbatim Transcription

**PROVA DE ESFORÇO**

ECG Basal: Ritmo sinusal. ECG sem alterações significativas.

| Parâmetro | Valor |
|---|---|
| Tempo de prova | 4 m 26 s |
| Fase | 2 |
| Protocolo | BRUCE |
| Capacidade funcional | Diminuída |
| Velocidade | 6.3 |
| Inclinação | METS |

| | BASAL | EXERCÍCIO | RECUPERAÇÃO |
|---|---|---|---|
| FREQUÊNCIA CARDÍACA (bpm) | 76 | 117 | (not fully legible) |
| PRESSÃO ARTERIAL (mmHg) | 166 / 70 | 110 / 64 | 118 / 70 |
| DUPLO PRODUTO | 7800 | 13670 | |

Motivo de interrupção: Sintomatologia habitual
Tempo de recuperação: 1m 30s

Ritmo: Sem alterações
Resposta Cronotrópica: Adequada

**Relatório:**

ECG REPOUSO (EM ORTOSTATISMO):
Ritmo sinusal. ECG sem alterações significativas.

TESTE DE ESFORÇO:
Iniciou esforço em tapete rolante, segundo o protocolo de Bruce, interrompeu aos 04 m 26 min por sintomas habituais (astenia; sensação de desfalecimento), tendo atingido a frequência cardíaca de 117 por minuto (63% da frequência cardíaca máxima prevista para o atleta). 6.3 MET(S).
Resposta hemodinâmica discutível (com queda de TA da fase 1 para a fase 2 durante o exercício).
Resposta tensional terminal, nomeadamente sem queda tensional com esforço.
FC atingida insuficiente.

RECUPERAÇÃO:
Manteve posição na posição de Trendelenburg durante 2 minutos (estando sempre) perfusão periférica adequada.
Sem alterações do ritmo e segmento ST. Suave a recuperação.
Ministrou-se subQ Glucagon no fim do 3 minuto, sem alterações de FC com sinais/sintomas.

**CONCLUSÃO:**

CPN: [Cardiologista B (Porto)]
Dr. [Cardiologista C (Porto)]

---

> **Note:** Some values in the table were partially legible from the screenshots. The 15 remaining photos (01 50 28 through 01 52 21) contain ECG tracings at various stages of the test — basal, exercise phases, and recovery.

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> **Exercise Stress Test (Bruce Protocol)**
>
> - **Duration:** 4 min 26 sec, Phase 2 — **functional capacity diminished**
> - **Max HR:** 117 bpm (63% of predicted max — insufficient)
> - Stopped due to habitual symptoms (asthenia, sensation of fainting)
> - **Questionable haemodynamic response** — BP drop from phase 1 to phase 2 during exercise
> - No terminal BP drop with exertion
> - Recovery: Trendelenburg position for 2 min, subQ Glucagon administered at 3 min
> - No rhythm or ST segment abnormalities
> - **Key finding: Diminished functional capacity with inadequate chronotropic response and questionable BP response during exercise**



---

# Carta Médica — Cardiologista A (London) — Tradução PT — 04-03-2026

**Data da consulta:** 04 de março de 2026 (teleconsulta)
**Paciente:** Patient
**Cardiologista:** Cardiologista A (London) — Cardiologista Consultora
**Tipo:** Tradução portuguesa da carta original em inglês (Patient Letter 06-03-2026)

---

## Nota

Este ficheiro é a tradução portuguesa da carta do Cardiologista A (London) datada de 04-03-2026. O conteúdo clínico é idêntico à versão inglesa transcrita em `Transcripts/2026/03-March/Cardiology/Patient-Letter-Cardiologist-A-London-2026-03-04.md`.

A versão portuguesa inclui clarificações adicionais do paciente sobre a carta original, nomeadamente:

- **TC Torácica / Angio-TAC (06/09/2021) - Hospital A (Porto):** Excluiu tromboembolismo pulmonar (TEP). Sem alterações parenquimatosas pulmonares significativas.
- **TC Pescoço (14/09/2021) - Hospital A (Porto):** Identificou formação nodular adjacente ao côndilo occipital esquerdo (~16x14 mm), com captação hipervascular, colocando-se a hipótese de malformação vascular / possível aneurisma de V3 da artéria vertebral esquerda.
- **RM crânio-encefálica com espectroscopia (17/09/2021) - Hospital A (Porto):** Identificou lesão inespecífica justacortical temporal mesial direita, centrada no giro lingual (~8 mm), possivelmente gliótica antiga, sem características de agressividade. A espectroscopia excluiu sinais de proliferação celular, perda neuronal ou metabolismo anaeróbio. A hipótese de quisto neuroepitelial foi considerada menos provável.
- **Angio-TC cerebral (23/09/2021) - Hospital A (Porto):** Excluiu aneurismas ou ectasias vasculares no segmento V3 da artéria vertebral esquerda. A formação previamente identificada corresponde a fenestração com drenagem para o lago venoso suboccipital, sem significado patológico.

O conteúdo restante é tradução directa. Consultar a versão inglesa para a transcrição completa.

---

## FILE: Transcripts Anonymous/2026/03-March/Cardiology/Patient-Letter-Cardiologist-A-London-2026-03-04.md

title: Patient Letter Cardiologist A 2026-03-04

# Patient Letter — Cardiologist A (London) — 04-03-2026

**Clinic Date:** 04 March 2026 (video consultation)
**Paciente:** Patient
**Cardiologist:** Cardiologist A (London) — Consultant Cardiologist
**Type:** Patient letter following video consultation

---

## Verbatim Transcription

Clinic Date: 04 March 2026 at [Clinic B (London)]

Mr Patient
[ADDRESS REMOVED]

Dear Mr Patient

Thank you very much for taking the time to meet with me via video consultation while you are in Portugal.

I was sorry to hear about the challenges you are currently facing, particularly caring for your mother who has dementia, as well as the other personal matters you mentioned.

Below is a summary of the key points from our discussion.

**Medical History and Known Conditions**

1. **Low Blood Pressure (Hypotension)**
You report having had naturally low blood pressure since a young age and have experienced several fainting episodes in the past.

2. **Bipolar Affective Disorder (diagnosed 2018)**
In 2022, possibly following COVID vaccination, you developed symptoms including parkinsonism, discoordinated movements, memory difficulties, and twitching while taking lamotrigine (Lamictal) and quetiapine. After switching to lithium, these symptoms resolved.

3. **Possible Post-Vaccine ME/CFS–like Syndrome**
Since 2024 you have been experiencing significant unexplained fatigue.
After receiving the Johnson & Johnson COVID vaccine in 2021, you developed symptoms including sleep apnoea and experienced a fainting episode. At that time you attended the emergency department where:
- A **D-dimer** was elevated.
- A **CT pulmonary angiogram** was performed, which ruled out pulmonary embolism.
- A CT scan of the brain also identified **gliosis**.

4. **Possible Lithium-Related Diabetes Insipidus**
Lithium was introduced and gradually increased under close psychiatric supervision in both Portugal and the UK. Your lithium levels have remained within therapeutic range and have not been toxic. However, there may be an element of diabetes insipidus related to lithium therapy.

**Current Medication and Supplements**

You reported currently taking:
- Lithium
- Two electrolyte packets daily
- Magnesium
- Vitamin D
- Vitamin B12
- Coenzyme Q10
- Omega-3
- Calcium
- Approximately 6 g of salt daily

You do not smoke and do not drink alcohol.

**You reported the following symptoms:**
- Fainting episode following vaccination in 2021
- Bradycardia during sleep
- Reduced exercise tolerance (previously able to walk approximately one mile daily)
- Significant fatigue, especially after activity
- Episodes of palpitations and chest pain
- Symptoms sometimes worsen after eating
- No clear orthostatic intolerance
- No heat intolerance; in fact, you felt significantly better during a recent trip to Brazil

You also reported laboratory tests suggesting **low plasma osmolality**. After discussing your symptoms with your psychiatrist and reviewing information independently, you increased your salt and fluid intake, which initially improved your symptoms. More recently, reducing water intake appears to have led to further improvement. For example, on a recent day you reported **fluid intake of approximately 3 L with urine output of about 3.7 L**.

**Previous Investigations (as discussed)**

You mentioned having undergone several investigations, including:

1. **Cardiac investigations** — It would be helpful to clarify exactly what tests were performed. In particular, I would like to know whether you have had: Troponin or NT-proBNP testing, an ECG, a recent Holter monitor. I am not overly concerned about episodes of bradycardia during sleep, as this can often be a sign of good cardiovascular fitness.

2. **CT scan of the chest**, possibly suggesting a clot in the neck.

3. **MRI of the brain with spectroscopy**, which confirmed gliosis but did not reveal any specific metabolic abnormalities.

**Clinical Impression**

At this stage, my impression is that you may be experiencing **dysautonomia**, potentially related to prior COVID infection or vaccination.

There may also be an element of **diabetes insipidus**, which could be related to lithium therapy even at relatively low doses. You appear to be particularly sensitive to medications, which is important to consider when planning treatment.

For this reason, I would prefer to minimise the introduction of additional medications wherever possible.

**Recommended Further Evaluation**

To ensure that we are not overlooking another underlying condition, I recommend the following:

1. **Autoimmune screening blood tests**, if these have not been done recently.

2. **Updated cardiovascular assessment**, including:
   - ECG
   - 24-hour blood pressure monitoring
   - Holter monitor
   This would help rule out any potential cardiac effects of lithium.

3. **Assessment of possible diabetes insipidus**, including:
   - Plasma osmolality
   - Serum sodium
   - Urine osmolality

I would recommend that these results be reviewed with either an **endocrinologist** or **internal medicine specialist** to help optimise your fluid and salt intake.

**Possible Treatment Considerations**

Depending on the results of the above assessments and your blood pressure readings, medications such as **fludrocortisone** or **midodrine** could potentially be considered to help:
- Maintain slightly higher blood pressure
- Improve sodium balance

However, this should only be considered after further evaluation.

**Lifestyle Recommendations**

I would encourage you to:
- Gradually reintroduce **gentle exercise**, such as short walks or yoga.
- Try to **leave the house at least once daily** where possible.
- Maintain **regular social interaction with family and friends**, as face-to-face contact can play an important role in wellbeing during prolonged illness.

Please feel free to contact me once you have the results of the recommended investigations. I will be happy to review them and help guide the next steps in your management.

Thank you again for your trust in consulting me.

Yours sincerely

[Cardiologist A (London)]
Consultant Cardiologist

---

# Referral Letter — Cardiologist A (London) to Neurologist C (London) — 24-03-2026

**Date:** 24th March 2026
**From:** [Cardiologist A (London)] — Consultant Cardiologist
**To:** [Neurologist C (London)]
**Re:** Patient

---

## Verbatim Transcription

Dear [Neurologist C],

I would be grateful if you could kindly assess this patient who presents with a complex constellation of neurological and systemic symptoms, including features raising the possibility of parkinsonism, although the overall clinical picture remains atypical.

I met him once during a video call from Portugal where he was with his family. I understand he is now back in London

This patient has a background of longstanding hypotension with prior syncopal episodes, and Bipolar Affective Disorder (diagnosed 2018). In 2022, while taking lamotrigine and quetiapine, they developed symptoms suggestive of parkinsonism, including discoordinated movements, memory impairment, and twitching. These symptoms resolved following a switch to lithium, suggesting a possible medication-related phenomenon at that time.

However, since 2024, the patient reports a recurrence of concerning symptoms, including:

- Reduced exercise tolerance (previously able to walk approximately one mile daily)
- Significant fatigue, particularly post-exertional
- Episodes of palpitations and chest pain
- Intermittent worsening of symptoms after meals
- Bradycardia during sleep
- A prior fainting episode following COVID vaccination in 2021

There is no clear orthostatic intolerance, and notably, the patient reports improvement in symptoms in warmer climates (e.g. during a recent trip to Brazil).

Additional background includes possible post-vaccine ME/CFS-like illness and suspected dysautonomia. There is also a question of lithium-related diabetes insipidus, with reported low plasma osmolality and high fluid turnover (e.g. ~3 L intake with ~3.7 L urine output), with some symptomatic improvement following adjustment of fluid and salt intake.

Investigations to date include:

- CT pulmonary angiogram (2021) – no pulmonary embolism (despite elevated D-dimer)
- CT and MRI brain (with spectroscopy) – showing gliosis without specific metabolic abnormality
- Cardiac investigations (details unclear; further clarification pending)

Current medications include lithium, electrolyte supplementation, magnesium, vitamin D, vitamin B12, coenzyme Q10, omega-3, calcium, and a high salt intake (~6 g daily). The patient does not smoke or consume alcohol.

While dysautonomia remains a possible unifying diagnosis, the history of prior parkinsonian features, together with ongoing fatigue, discoordination, and cognitive symptoms, raises concern about a possible underlying or evolving neurological disorder that would benefit from specialist assessment. He recently had another episode of dystonia (he shared with me videos which I could not review), this sounds very atypical of ME/dysautonomia.

I would be very grateful for your expert opinion regarding:

- Whether these symptoms may represent a form of parkinsonism or other movement disorder
- The relevance of prior medication-induced symptoms
- Any further neurological investigations that may be indicated

Please do not hesitate to contact me if further information would be helpful.

Yours sincerely

[Cardiologist A (London)]
Consultant Cardiologist

## FILE: Transcripts Anonymous/2026/03-March/Health-Log/Diario-de-Saude-Fadiga-Distonia-2024-2026.md

---

# Diário de Saúde — Fadiga to Distonia — 2024-2026

**Started:** 11.03.2026
**Author:** Patient (self-authored patient diary)

---

## Verbatim Transcription

**Diário de Saude**
Started 11.03.2026

**Medicação Inicial - 2022-2025:**
Lítio 600mg
Seroquel 50mg

**Suplementos:** Nenhums

**Níveis de energia:**
Normais com estranhas faltas de energia em Março
3-4 horas de fadiga extrema em Setembro 2025
Dificuldade em sair da cama / sofá em Janeiro 2026
Recuperação rápida com suplementação de 4-6g de sal dissolvido em água - dividido em 2x ou 3x doses por dia. Inicialmente 2g sal em 400ml de água, depois reduzido para 2g sal em 200ml de água.

**Relato:**

Em Março de 2025 ano tinha dias contínuos a trabalhar sem grandes problemas.
Pelo Verão de 2025 já tinha fadiga acentuada e estratégias de compensação. Recuperava com exercício e 1-2 horas de luz solar (fazia exercício ao ar livre). No Verão fiz bastante caminhadas com peso, caminhava 1.5km com 16 a 24kg adicionados, sendo o meu peso na altura 80kg. Sentia que o Sol + exercício ajudava. Existia alguma fadiga, estranha.
Inicialmente associei os sintomas ao bipolar. Acabou por ser difícil manter esta associação após Janeiro de 2026, com a introdução de 4-6g de sal dissolvido em água em 2x a 3x doses diárias, e a resolução praticamente imediata (40-90min.) da fadiga - e da raiva inexplicada até então.

**Setembro de 2025 (est.)**

Comecei a tomar magnésio e Vitamina D quando foi primeiro detectado a sua potencial ausência num teste de sangue feito pelo laboratório [Laboratório A] (que era mínima mas decidi precaver). Estava a fazer testes em coordenação com o meu Psiquiatra para investigar a razão para a fadiga e falta de energia que me vinha a afligir desde 2024.

A introdução de suplementos de magnésio e Vitamina D por volta de Setembro de 2025 parece colmatar o que se passava. Senti-me, durante algum tempo, bastante melhor.

Estimo na altura 266mg de magnésio e 8000 IU de Vitamina D - Doses Diárias. São ambos os suplementos da Solgar.

A fadiga por volta desta altura já é bastante acentuada. Isto significa, já em Setembro/Outubro, talvez 3 a 4 horas passados em cama a recuperar. Depois de passar algum tempo (45 min a 1 hora) na cama, recuperava, continuava a trabalhar. Com os suplementos, isto reduz-se, mas não desaparece. E gradualmente, os suplementos perdem eficácia, embora isso só se torne óbvio em Janeiro de 2026.

Tinha também a questão da raiva. A partir de certa hora, sentia uma "mudança" e havia uma alteração na minha capacidade de tolerar as coisas. Inicialmente achei que a raiva poderia ter alguma relação com a bipolaridade. Mas era "diferente", vinha em certa hora, sentia "pressão" a subir pela espinha até à parte de trás da cabeça. E a partir dessa hora, era díficil "esquecer" qualquer coisa que me irritava. A pressão na cabeça estava alterada, sentia isso fisicamente. Havia pressão à volta da parte de cima da cabeça, pela testa e pela região nesta zona, pela parte de trás da cabeça e pela parte de trás do pescoço. Era como uma ativação. E sentia que algo químico se tinha alterado, e a partir desse ponto as coisas só pioravam - era difícil lidar com qualquer desafio sem algum descontrolo. Estava sempre no limite. Conseguia isolar-me e trabalhar pois trabalho remotamente.

Como os ataques de raiva pareciam-me subir em número e gravidade quando tirava o Seroquel, mantive-o em conjunto com o lítio. Ou seja, desde 2022 (e da crise distônica que levou ao abandono como fármaco principal) a medicação ficou igual, com algumas tentativas de sair do Seroquel apenas, que depois de 2022 estava também apenas em 50mg.*

Durante grande parte deste tempo, a combinação de raiva + fadiga fez-me pensar que isto se tratava de uma questão relacionada com o bipolar, com depressão bipolar e raiva bipolar. Contudo a introdução de água com sal em Janeiro de 2026 remove os 2 problemas - comprovados com tanto redução da fadiga, como também é eficaz em "acabar" com um ataque de raiva. Questiona-se assim a relação com a bipolaridade, pois não vejo razão para a bipolaridade ser afetada por ingestão de água com sal.

Vou para o Brazil em Dezembro. Fadiga/baixa energia continua. Suplementação parece reduzir o problema, mas não o resolve.

*Registo Histórico: Medicação 2018-2022 - Seroquel SR - 300mg - Lamictal / Lamotrigina - não me recordo bem da dose, mas talvez 150mg. Alterado para Lítio 600mg e Seroquel 50mg após crise distônica.*

**Dezembro/Janeiro 2026**

No Brazil fico sem os suplementos. Durante algum tempo parece-me ok. Parece-me que no Brazil, onde é Verão, e há sol, e estou de férias.
Mas eventualmente os sintomas retornam e fico sem suplementos Solgar que trouxe comigo de Portugal, vou e compro Magnésio e Vitamina D localmente. Talvez de baixa qualidade.
Sinto melhoria também a tomar água de coco - em conjunto com os suplementos.
Certamente os suplementos não são tão eficazes, mas consigo trabalhar.

**Retorno a Portugal em Janeiro 2026**

Poucos dias após o retorno os sintomas agravam-se. Estou no meu pior estado. A maior parte do dia é no sofá ou na cama a descansar. Fico com preocupação sobre manter o meu emprego. A situação torna-se grave o suficiente que já não sei como me manter útil.

Reparo que quando me sento fico pior ainda. Parece que vou adormecer. Transformo a minha secretária numa standing desk para conseguir continuar a trabalhar.

**Mais grave: quando vou fazer exercício (pela primeira vez vou ao exterior fazer exercício em meses, devido à chuva), sinto que vou adormecer ou ter um blackout.**

Volto para casa. É aí que, numa tentativa de perceber o que se passa, (já não tolero exercício) faço pesquisas sobre a minha condição - e uma sugestão aparece - tomar sal dissolvido em água. 2g em 400ml.

Faço isso. Tomo 2g de sal em 400ml, tudo duma vez em 2-3 min. e o meu cansaço desaparece em uma hora. Diria que em 60 min. estou funcional. Em 15-30 min. já senti uma diferença enorme.

Pouco depois continuo a pesquisar. A raiva pode ser cortisol. Faço o teste. Deixo aparecer um episódio de raiva (na altura ainda comuns). Tomo o sal diretamente em cima do episódio. Ele desaparece.

**Tanto a raiva quanto o cansaço são diretamente afetados pela introdução do Sal.**

**Fim de Janeiro 2026**

Formulei por volta desta altura **um plano mais agressivo de suplementação.**

De fim de Janeiro 2026 até 8 de Março 2026 - Doses Diárias:
- Pure EPA Omega 3 - 1000mg
- Fairvital B2 - Vitamin B2 - 93mg + L-leucin - 120 mg
- Calcium citrate - 1000mg
- Bysglicinato de magnésio - 900mg
- Magnesium L-Threonate - 500mg
- Vitamin D3 (essential nutrition) - 6000 IU
- Vitamin D3/K2 Combinado - Vitamina D3 2000 IU / Vitamina K2 100ug
- Magnésio que Dissolve do Pingo Doce - 375mg
- Vitamina C - 1000mg
- 2x sacos de Dioralyte (2x ao dia)
- CoQ10 - 400mg
- E 6 gramas de sal. Inicialmente em 400ml. Depois em 200ml quando é encontrada a poliúria (4.3L e 5.6L).

USADOS MAS INTERROMPIDOS:
- Vitamin B12 - Methylcobalamin - 1000mg (2-3 dias, parou — "fez-me sentir estranho")
- NAC - 600 to 300mg (2-3 semanas, interrompido)

Por volta da mesma altura — **removo o Seroquel completamente, com conhecimento do meu psiquiatra.**

**Nova Crise Distônica**

Estamos no início de Março. A fadiga parece estar a reduzir. Mas a distonia, que causou a crise em 2022, parece estar a voltar.

*Na realidade a distonia nunca desapareceu desde 2022, mas a sua presença era muito muito pouco acentuada. A partir da primeira semana de Março, volta com uma força que não existia desde 2022.*

**9 de Março de 2026**

Em 9 de Março de 2026 há nova crise distônica. A progressão culminou num episódio grave — movimentos involuntários violentos nos braços e mãos, ardor e formigueiro na parte de trás e nas laterais da cabeça e uma sensação generalizada que só posso descrever como o meu corpo «em chamas».

Nota: *O episódio de distonia aguda de 2022 ocorreu com Seroquel 300 mg e lamotrigina e foi atribuído ao medicamento. Continuei então com uma dose baixa de Seroquel (50-25 mg) durante aproximadamente 3 anos. Pouco antes deste episódio, interrompo completamente os últimos 25 mg há apenas algumas semanas.*

Sobre a distonia, observei:
- Não está presente pela manhã, após acordar
- Começa à tarde e piora ao longo da noite
- Deitar proporciona alívio parcial
- Retomar Seroquel 50 mg proporcionou alívio significativo

No dia da crise: 20mg de cetirizina + 50mg de Seroquel.
Dias seguintes: adicionou Telfast 180mg de manhã + 20mg Famotidina pela noite.

**Exames BP/HR (home measurements):**

Supine (~10 min): ~104/65, HR 57 | ~103/64, HR 56
Standing: 1min 103/66 HR 71 | 4-5min 107/69 HR 69 | 10min 109/71 HR 71
Symptomatic later: 96/60, HR 66
Post-prandial symptomatic: ~101/67, HR 72

**Log de Urina:**
- 24 Feb 2026: 1a urina 1.7L
- 08/04/2026: 1a urina 1.4L - no night urine
- 09/04/2026: 1a urina 1L - no night urine

**13 Março 2026:** Urina praticamente branca/transparente. Sem sensação no perineo. **Numb.**
**14 Março 03:00am:** Scrotum pain quite bad. Always seems to get worse at night in bed.

**Novo plano de suplementação (pós-crise):**
- Vitamin D3 - 4000 IU
- Vitamin D3/K2 Combinado - D3 2000 IU / K2 100ug
- Magnesium L-Threonate - 1000mg
- Pure EPA Omega 3 - 1000mg
- 2x sacos de Dioralyte
- 2g de sal em 200ml 3x ao dia

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> Detailed 7-page patient health diary covering the progression from fatigue (2024) through dystonia crisis (March 2026). Key observations:
> - **Salt water (2g in 400ml) resolves both fatigue AND rage episodes within 30-60 minutes** — questions bipolar attribution
> - Progressive fatigue worsening: March 2025 (mild) → Sept 2025 (3-4h/day) → Jan 2026 (bed-bound, exercise intolerance with near-blackout)
> - Mg + Vit D supplementation helped initially (Sept 2025) but gradually lost efficacy
> - Brazil trip (Dec-Jan): improved with sun/heat, worsened on return to Portugal
> - **Seroquel discontinuation (early March) → progressive dystonia return → acute crisis 9 March 2026**
> - Dystonia pattern: absent mornings, worsens afternoon→night, lying down helps
> - Home BP/HR: low baseline (~103/64), adequate orthostatic response, drops to 96/60 when symptomatic
> - **Perineal numbness + scrotal pain** documented 13-14 March (preceding the cauda equina-like ER visit)
> - Polyuria documented: first morning urine volumes 1.0-1.7L

# Patient Letter — Neurologist C (London) — 27-03-2026

**Date:** 27/03/2026
**Paciente:** Patient
**Neurologist:** Neurologist C (London) — Consultant Neurologist
**Type:** Patient letter following consultation

---

## Verbatim Transcription

27/03/2026

Mr Patient
[ADDRESS REMOVED]

Dear Mr Cardoso

Re:
N: Patient DOB: [DOB REMOVED]
A: [ADDRESS REMOVED]
E: [EMAIL REMOVED]
M: [PHONE REMOVED]

**Diagnosis:**
1. Functional Neurological Disorder - F44.4
2. Bipolar Affective Disorder (2018) - F31.9
3. Obstructive Sleep Apnoea (2022) - G47.33
4. Profound Fatigue - R53.83
5. Polyuria with stated renal concentrating defect - R35

**Current medications:**
1. Lithium 600 mg daily
2. Seroquel (quetiapine) 50 mg daily

**Recommendations:**
1. Please continue management under your current psychiatrist and renal physician.
2. It would be helpful to review correspondence from your cardiologist.
3. An MRI of the whole neuraxis is scheduled for the end of April, but I do not feel there is an urgency for this.

Many thanks for coming to see me today. You are now 36 years old and you work in advertising. You are right handed.

I explained that I am using software (Heidi AI) to record the consultation, allowing me to accurately capture medical information.

You came to see me because you have been experiencing worsening fatigue, which began in 2025, and intermittent abnormal movements.

**Presenting Problem:**

You described the main problem as a profound fatigue that has been worsening throughout 2025, progressing to a state of 'complete collapse' that significantly impacts your ability to work. You described the fatigue as a lack of energy and a feeling of sleepiness. Previously, sleep would alleviate this, but it has become more persistent.

Initial tests for your thyroid and kidney function were normal. In late 2025, you found some improvement after taking magnesium, calcium, and vitamin D supplements. During a trip to Brazil for New Year's, your symptoms improved, but they returned about a week after your supplements ran out. On returning to Portugal on 12/01/2026, you experienced a significant deterioration.

A key feature you reported is exercise intolerance. You mentioned that you used to walk a mile each morning with a 24 kg pack, but when you attempted to resume this, you felt as if you were going to black out and became sleepier, which was unprecedented for you. Following a suggestion from an AI assistant, you tried taking 2g of salt in 400ml of water and found that your fatigue completely resolved within 30-40 minutes.

You also told me about abnormal movements that first appeared in 2022 while you were on quetiapine. You described these as generalised, flailing movements of your upper body, head, neck, and trunk, particularly when making intentional movements like putting on a jacket. These episodes were continuous and were associated with significant short-term memory impairment. Both the movements and memory loss resolved when you stopped quetiapine.

However, similar movements have returned recently. You said they are intermittent, seem to be related to stress, and worsen as the day goes on. The recent re-emergence on 09/03/2026 was preceded by an episode of painful, needle-like sensations around your buttocks, followed by violent jerking. This occurred after you had recently stopped taking a low dose of quetiapine, which you had been on for several years.

Around 13/03/2026, you experienced an episode of what you described as cauda equina-like symptoms, with complete perineal and scrotal anaesthesia, leg weakness, and lower back pain. This led to a hospital admission in Portugal, where your symptoms reportedly improved with diazepam.

**Past Medical Problems:**

You have a diagnosis of bipolar affective disorder, which was made in 2018. You also have obstructive sleep apnoea, diagnosed in 2022, for which you use a CPAP machine. You fractured your right fifth metatarsal in November 2021. You believe you may have had an adverse reaction to the Janssen COVID-19 vaccine in August 2021, with an onset of sensory disturbance on the right side of your body, weakness, and the start of your sleep apnoea. In November 2022, you had an episode of acute dystonia or akathisia, which was attributed to quetiapine at the time and was associated with significant short-term memory loss. This resolved when you switched from quetiapine to lithium.

**Current Medications:**

You are currently taking Lithium 600 mg daily and Seroquel (quetiapine) 50 mg daily. You mentioned that the quetiapine was recently stopped and then restarted after the abnormal movements re-emerged. Your lithium levels are checked regularly and have been persistently subtherapeutic but psychiatrically effective. You have no known drug allergies.

**Family History:**

You reported no known family history of neurological disease.

**Social History:**

You work in advertising, which you describe as a high-stress job with long hours. You are currently working remotely from Portugal, where you are the sole carer for your mother who has dementia. You have not consumed alcohol for the past year and are a non-smoker. You reported no recreational drug use in the last two years. You previously exercised daily but are currently unable to due to profound exercise-induced fatigue. You told me your sleep is good when you use your CPAP machine.

**Physical Examination:**

On observation today, there were brief, intermittent episodes of forward truncal flexion and jerking. I also noted a sudden jerk, similar to an exaggerated startle response, when I touched your head.

The examination of your cranial nerves was normal. Your pupils were equal and reactive to light, and you have a full range of eye movements. Your facial sensation and muscle power were normal. Your speech was normal.

Examination of your arms was normal. Muscle tone was normal and power was full (5/5 on the MRC scale) in all muscle groups tested, including your shoulders, biceps, triceps, wrists, and hands. Your coordination, tested with finger-nose testing and rapid alternating movements, was normal. Your reflexes in your arms were present and symmetrical. Sensation to light touch and vibration appeared intact in your hands.

Examination of your legs was also normal. Muscle tone was normal and power was full (5/5 on the MRC scale) in all muscle groups tested, including your hips, knees, and ankles. Your reflexes at the knees and ankles were present and symmetrical, and your plantar responses were downgoing. Sensation to vibration was normal in your toes.

In summary, your neurological examination was essentially normal, apart from the minimal, intermittent, non-stereotyped jerking movements observed.

**Summary and Management Plan:**

The clinical picture, with profound fatigue and intermittent, fluctuating abnormal movements, is complex. Your neurological examination today is largely reassuring.

The abnormal movements you are experiencing are not typical for a drug-induced movement disorder, given their paroxysmal and fluctuating nature. The overall presentation is most consistent with a functional neurological disorder (FND). This is a condition where the 'software' of the nervous system is not working correctly, despite the 'hardware' being structurally intact. FND often occurs in the context of other stressors, such as your high-pressure job and caring responsibilities, and underlying conditions like bipolar disorder. The fatigue is likely multifactorial, with contributions from the FND and your underlying psychiatric condition. The cauda equina-like episode is also likely part of the FND, given that imaging has not shown a structural cause and the symptoms have resolved.

At this time, I do not recommend any new medications for the movement disorder. I have suggested potentially testing for an acetylcholine receptor antibody blood test to rule out myasthenia gravis, which is an uncommon cause of fluctuating weakness, although I anticipate this will be negative as you have no clinical signs of the condition.

I advised you to continue with your current management under your psychiatrist and renal physician. The most effective treatment for FND is often a multi-disciplinary approach, primarily involving management of the underlying psychiatric condition through talking therapies and appropriate medication, alongside developing cognitive strategies to manage the functional symptoms. It is a clinical diagnosis based on the pattern of symptoms and signs, as there is no specific test for it.

The benefit of this plan is to avoid the risks of unnecessary investigations while acknowledging the risk, albeit low, that a subtle underlying organic cause could be missed. An alternative would be to pursue more aggressive testing immediately, but this is not felt to be clinically indicated given the extensive negative workup to date.

You have my email and can contact me with any questions and if any of your symptoms change or you are concerned in any way.

Yours sincerely

[Neurologist C (London)]
Consultant Neurologist

---

## Verbatim Transcription

**From:** [Psiquiatra B (Porto)]
**Date:** Mon 2026-03-16 4:26 PM
**To:** Patient

Boa tarde Patient,

Lamento saber da situação. Espero que esteja melhor.
É bastante informação, pelo que peço desde já desculpa se não conseguir esclarecer todas as suas questões.
Tentando ir por partes:

1. Confirmo que o Patient tem aderido ao tratamento desde o início do acompanhamento comigo e que, mesmo com níveis de Lítio relativamente baixos, tem-se mantido razoavelmente estável, ou seja, sem episódios depressivos ou maníacos graves (pode usar este email como prova). Sabemos que os níveis de Lítio são dependentes de muitas variáveis de pessoa para pessoa e mesmo na própria pessoa ao longo do tempo. Sabemos também que, embora os estudos demonstrem eficácia em níveis acima de 0.6, muitos doentes mantêm-se estáveis com doses menores.

2. Ainda que não tenha observado os sintomas do episódio actual, confirmo também que em 2022 apresentou movimentos involuntários que foram caracterizados pelo neurologista que o observou na altura como distónicos/parkinsónicos (pode também usar como prova).

3. É possível que a diurese aumentada esteja a levar a diminuição dos níveis séricos de lítio. O lítio "acompanha" a excreção de urina e daí a recomendação de manter uma boa hidratação quando se faz lítio, para evitar um cenário de retenção e intoxicação. No entanto, o inverso também pode acontecer - caso muita urina seja excretada, os níveis podem baixar.

4. Dependendo do que o resultado das análises que fez hoje ao Lítio, devemos reconsiderar a terapêutica. Aumentar o Seroquel é uma hipótese mas gostaria de ter o resultado das análises antes de decidir.

Cumprimentos

---

**Email original do paciente (sábado, 14/03/2026 às 21:33):**

Olá Dr. [Psiquiatra B],

Infelizmente a minha situação complica-se.

A fadiga alterou-se e agora senti a distonia a voltar. Para estabilidade decidi voltar ao que estava - 600mg de Lítio e 50mg de Seroquel.

Já fui ao endocrinologista que pediu imensos testes, que estão em curso. Também se está a investigar disfunção autonómica, o que está a ser feito com o cardiologista [Cardiologista B] no Hospital A (Porto). Já fiz um teste de ECG sobre pressão e vou fazer mais testes esta semana.

Resumindo tenho agora os seguintes sintomas:
- distonia / Parkinsonismo (como viu em 2022) que retornou
- A tal fadiga parece menos presente, continuo a tomar o sal compensatório (4-6g ao dia)
- A partir de 2a feira, comecei a sentir formigueiro doloroso como senti na altura do COVID em 2021.

Contudo isto complica-se.

- Ontem pela noite, tinha cada vez menos vontade de dormir pois - perdi alguma sensação à volta dos genitais - ardia-me naquele formigueiro doloroso a parte interior das pernas à volta dos genitais.

E então liguei ao SNS 24 que me recomendou as urgências. Fui até ao CUF Porto, onde tenho plano CUF.

O resultado disto foi questionável. Só li as notas de alta que são

- como falei em disfunção autonómica, que está a ser investigada pelo próprio CUF, isso parece ter removido a objetividade dos médicos presentes, que consideraram isso fabuloso (é realmente raro numa pessoa da minha idade).
- como tinha a distonia / Parkinsonismo que o Dr já presenciou em 2022, parecem ter assumido que estava em drogas ou álcool (testaram para isso - e deu em 0)
- como o resultado do lítio saiu pouco detetável, assumiram que não estou a fazer tratamento e estava maníaco e a inventar sintomas. (Envio os resultados dos testes em anexo)
- como pedi diazepam pois não me sentia bem e ajudou em 2021/2022, registaram tudo como um episódio de ansiedade, mania e psiquiátrico.

Em suma, como o Dr. sabe nunca tive ideia nem nunca tentei escapar ao tratamento para a bipolaridade. Desde que nos conhecemos que nunca tentei escapar ao tratamento nem tenho intenção disso pois sei muito bem das consequências e como podem ser fatais.

Liguei hoje ao CUF a informar que não achava que aquilo era correto (na altura ninguém me explicou nada, eu adormeci, trocou-se o turno da médica que me deram entrada, e deram-me alta imediatamente sem me explicar o porquê). Mas pedia lhe um favor e duas perguntas:

- seria possível enviar uma carta a clarificar 1. Que concordamos já há muitos anos que o nível sub terapêutico do lítio mantém-me estável o suficiente e e decidimos manter ? Estou continuamente a receber perguntas sobre isso e isso causa demasiadas dúvidas. 2. Que nunca tentei "escapar" ao tratamento da minha condição e que sempre tomei a medicação? Isso ajudava a clarificar este episódio bizarro e sequelas - caso tenha outro episódio de urgência prevenir que assumam novamente mania. 3. Que presenciou o episódio de distonia / Parkinsonismo em 2022 e que foi resolvido com o próprio Dr. a guiar na altura a alteração da medicação para Lítio?

Outra questão - tendo em conta os resultados do lítio que parecem ter diminuído até serem pouco detetáveis, devemos ajustar alguma coisa na terapia ? Como lhe disse já reintroduzi o Seroquel e parece ser moderador contra a distonia, como e porquê não tenho ideia. Não me importo em aumentar novamente o Seroquel para 150mg + 600mg de lítio se for preciso. **Mesmo se a distonia voltar, é preferível a ficar com mania. Mas tendo em conta a questão urinária, será que estou a manter os medicamentos no sistema a este ponto o suficiente para ser tratado para a bipolaridade efetivamente ? O que fazer?**

Ou seja, eu vou refazer estes testes ao lítio também na 2a feira. **Se se confirmar a descida de lítio para níveis muito baixos mesmo com 600mg, o que fazemos?** É possível então que o problema urinário signifique que os medicamentos já não ficam tempo suficiente no corpo para serem eficazes?

Agradeço qualquer clarificação quando puder
Patient

# Resumo Clínico — Por Favor Leia Antes de Avaliar (2026)

**Tipo:** Documento auto-preparado para apresentação em urgências
**Paciente:** Patient

---

## Verbatim Transcription

**RESUMO CLÍNICO — POR FAVOR LEIA ANTES DE AVALIAR**

**Nome:** Patient **DN:** [DOB REMOVED] | **Sexo:** M | **Nº Doente CUF:** [ID REMOVED]

**Diagnósticos conhecidos:** Perturbação afetiva bipolar (estável, seguido em psiquiatria) Apneia obstrutiva do sono (AHI 7, em CPAP) Disfunção autonómica em estudo (em seguimento com [Cardiologista B (Porto)], Hospital A (Porto)) Defeito de concentração renal associado a lítio (poliúria documentada ~4350ml/24h e ~5500ml/24h)

**Medicação atual:** Lítio 600mg | Quetiapina 50mg

**O que se passa comigo:** Tenho suspeita em investigação de uma doença do sistema nervoso autónomo em investigação desde 2024. Desde então, tenho tido sintomas progressivos como fadiga crónica, poliúria, perda de sensação e vários sintomas neurológicos que vão aparecendo ao longo do tempo.

Estou a ser seguido pelo [Cardiologista B (Porto)] (cardiologia autonómica, Hospital A (Porto)), que já pediu prova de esforço e teste de tilt table. Tenho também seguimento em psiquiatria ([Psiquiatra B (Porto)], [Clínica Psiquiatria A (Porto)]), nefrologia ([Nefrologista A (Porto)], [Clínica Nefrologia A]), e uma avaliação de cardiologia em Londres ([Cardiologista A (London)]).

**Nota sobre movimentos involuntários:** Tenho história de distonia / parkinsonismo medicamentosa documentada em novembro de 2022 no Hospital A (Porto) e pelo meu psiquiatra. Foi atribuída à medicação (quetiapina 300mg + lamotrigina) e tratada com Artane. Se apresentar estereotipias ou movimentos involuntários, estes são consistentes com esse antecedente — não com intoxicação ou uso de substâncias.

**Indico por favor:** Que sintomas neurológicos sejam avaliados como tal, independentemente do meu diagnóstico psiquiátrico. A minha doença bipolar está controlada. O nível de lítio pode aparecer baixo (<0.20-0.42) devido ao defeito renal de concentração documentado — não por falta de adesão à medicação.

**Contacto dos meus médicos assistentes:** [Cardiologista B (Porto)] — Hospital A (Porto), Cardiologia / Função Autonómica e [Psiquiatra B (Porto)], [Clínica Psiquiatria A (Porto)].

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> **Clinical Summary — Please Read Before Assessing**
>
> Self-prepared document for emergency presentations. Key points:
> - Known diagnoses: Bipolar disorder (stable), OSA (AHI 7, on CPAP), autonomic dysfunction under investigation, lithium-related renal concentrating defect (documented polyuria ~4350-5500ml/24h)
> - Current meds: Lithium 600mg, Quetiapine 50mg
> - Under investigation for autonomic nervous system disease since 2024 with progressive symptoms
> - History of documented drug-induced dystonia/parkinsonism (Nov 2022) — involuntary movements are consistent with this, not intoxication
> - Requests neurological symptoms be assessed independently of psychiatric diagnosis
> - Low lithium levels (<0.20-0.42) are due to renal concentrating defect, not non-compliance

# Data Files Index — Raw CSV/Device Data

These files contain raw device data and compilations. They are not traditional medical documents requiring verbatim transcription but are referenced here for completeness.

---

## Moodnotes Report
- **Source:** `Raw/Moodnotes Complete to 2025/MoodnotesReport.csv`
- **Type:** Mood tracking app export (CSV)
- **Date range:** Sept 2025 — Feb 2026 (14 entries visible)
- **Content:** Mood ratings (3-5 scale), incident notes documenting salt effects, supplement changes, anger episodes, nausea, brain fog, medication adjustments
- **Key entries:** Salt water resolving fatigue, anger after eating sugar/KitKat, nausea/dizziness Nov 2025, Seroquel withdrawal Oct 2025
- **PII:** None beyond first name in entries

## Test Results Compilation CSV
- **Source:** `Raw/Test Results 24-25-26/Test Results 2024-25 - Vertical 01 (1).csv`
- **Type:** Patient-compiled spreadsheet of lab results (CSV)
- **Date range:** Jul 2023 — Jan 2026
- **Content:** Consolidation of GS lab values (HbA1c, urea, creatinine, calcium, magnesium, Vit D, PTH, phosphate, ionised calcium, lithium, TSH, FT4, 1,25-dihydroxy Vit D, urinary iron) — all values already transcribed from individual lab PDFs
- **Note:** This is a **compilation**, not a duplicate — useful as a longitudinal tracking sheet

## O2Ring Sleep/Oximetry Records (Feb 2026)
- **Source:** `Raw/sleep records 2026/`
- **Type:** O2Ring pulse oximeter CSV exports + PDF summary reports
- **Files:**
  - Feb 01: `O2Ring_20260201021806.csv` + `.pdf`
  - Feb 02: `O2Ring_20260202001728.csv` + `.pdf`
  - Feb 03: `O2Ring_20260203234852.csv` + `.pdf`
  - Feb 04: `FEB 04 2026 - CPAP OSCAR DATA - document1.pdf` (CPAP data)
  - Lying down test: `O2Ring_20260202225120.csv` + `.pdf`
  - Standing test 2 min: `O2Ring_20260202225908.csv` + `.pdf`
  - Standing test 10 min: `O2Ring_20260202231110.csv` + `.pdf`
  - Root level duplicates of Feb 01 data
- **Content:** 4-second interval recordings of SpO2, pulse rate, motion. Baseline SpO2 ~95%, resting HR ~52-54 bpm
- **Standing tests:** Orthostatic HR/SpO2 monitoring (relevant to dysautonomia investigation)
- **PII:** None in CSV data

## Raw.md
- **Source:** `Raw/Raw.md`
- **Content:** Empty file (Obsidian placeholder)

## Claude Documents (in Raw/)
- **Source:** `Raw/Claude Documents/` (~15 PDFs)
- **Status:** Excluded from git (.gitignore). Not yet sanitised. AI-generated health summaries and research documents.

## CT-Brain-2018-02-27

*Source: `2018/02-February/Imaging/CT-Brain-2018-02-27.md`*

# TC Crânio-Encefálica — 27-02-2018

**Data:** 27-02-2018
**Paciente:** Patient
**Médico requisitante:** Médico Referente A (Guimarães)
**Instituição:** Centro de Imagiologia A (Guimarães)
**Médico relator:** Radiologista A (Guimarães)

---

## Verbatim Transcription

**INFORMAÇÃO CLÍNICA:** "Doente com patologia do foro psíquico. Para exclusão de doença orgânica."

**TC CRÂNIO-ENCEFÁLICA**

**TÉCNICA:**
Orientados por topograma digital lateral, efectuaram-se cortes tomográficos axiais de 2,5mm de espessura para estudo da fossa posterior e de 5mm de espessura para avaliação do compartimento supra-tentorial.

**RELATÓRIO:**

O parênquima encefálico não apresenta alteração morfológica ou densitométrica, focal ou difusa.

Não é visível lesão endocraniana com localização intra ou extra-axial, nomeadamente de natureza expansiva.

Sistemas basais, ventrículos, espaços cisternais e sulcos corticais cerebrais com forma e dimensões normais. Ausência de colecções peri-contraste.

Sem sinais de conflito ao nível do buraco occipital.

Não se observa lesão óssea localizada na calote ou na base do crânio.

Correcta apresentação dos seios peri-nasais e das cavidades antro-timpânicas e das células mastoideas.

---

> **English translation note:**
> 
> **Clinical information:** "Patient with psychiatric pathology. To exclude organic disease."
> 
> **Brain CT scan**
> 
> **Technique:** Guided by digital lateral topogram, axial CT slices of 2.5mm thickness for posterior fossa study and 5mm thickness for supratentorial compartment evaluation.
> 
> **Report:** Brain parenchyma shows no morphological or densitometric alteration, focal or diffuse. No visible intracranial lesion, intra- or extra-axial, namely of expansive nature. Basal systems, ventricles, cisternal spaces and cortical cerebral sulci with normal shape and dimensions. No peri-contrast collections. No signs of conflict at the occipital foramen level. No bone lesion in the calvarium or skull base. Normal presentation of paranasal sinuses, anterior-tympanic cavities and mastoid cells.

## GP-Letter-Psychiatrist-A-2019-03-08

*Source: `2019/03-March/Psychiatry/GP-Letter-Psychiatrist-A-2019-03-08.md`*

# GP Letter — Psychiatrist A (London) — 08-03-2019

**Clinic Date:** 8 March 2019
**Paciente:** Patient
**Psychiatrist:** Psychiatrist A (London) — Consultant Psychiatrist
**Addressed to:** GP Surgery A (London)
**Type:** Initial assessment — GP letter

---

## Verbatim Transcription

8 March 2019

Clinic Date: 8 March 2019

Dear Doctor

Re: Mr Patient [SURNAME REMOVED] - dob [DOB REMOVED]
[ADDRESS REMOVED]

I had the pleasure to meet today during my outpatients clinic at [Clinic A (London)] Mr Patient [SURNAME REMOVED].

At the time of our first meeting, Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] was taking Abilify 10mg, mane and Promethazine 50mg, nocte for a manic relapse of his bipolar disorder.

Today he comes to the clinic as afflicted by restlessness and asking for alternatives to current medications.

Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] recalls an hypomanic relapse in January 2019 when he started feeling easily irritated by people around him who he would find incredibly slow and would trigger violent thoughts about beating them up or punish them for being so slow. He also experienced racing thoughts, fluctuations in his mood with sudden changes from elation to low mood, increased sexual libido and overspending.

He asked to be reviewed by the public sector by was denied any urgent appointment. He then attended A&E and was given Abilify 10mg, mane but this gave him restlessness and increased appetite and was unable to work and carry on his normal life feeling so restless. He was recently taken on by home treatment team but has been discharged following a three days trip to Cologne to meet a woman he fell in love with.

He feels that Abilify has helped him and he can manage sleep with the Promethazine but it seems that he requires additional medications to aid with sleep, the racing thoughts have slightly dissipated and the violent thoughts have reduced; however, mood continues to fluctuate rapidly and still feel hypersexual and with a tendency to overspending. He specifies the sex is promiscuous but protected with consensual female adult partners met through phone apps. He denies any grandiose beliefs of delusional nature or any other psychotic symptom.

He is currently followed up by mental health services in [Borough] and [GP B (London)] in primary care. He was told that he had an appointment with the community mental health team on 18/03 but realised that he could not wait because of rapid deterioration of mental state.

**Past Psychiatric History**

Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] recalls a first manic episode in Feb 2018 following sentimental involvement with a woman. He thought he could see 'love' and thought he needed to start a new religion, he stopped sleeping, thought he was becoming a genius, started becoming hyper-religious going to Buddhist centre every day and then felt a 'detonation' after which he could see 'love', he could sense 'vibrations' coming out of living beings. After a while he began feeling unsafe with pressured speech and racing thoughts and started flooding the woman he was in love with text messages until she eventually recoiled and blocked him. Denies any auditory hallucination, thought broadcasting or insertion at the time.

He then recalls reading the symptoms of psychosis on the internet and recognising some of the features. He went to the GP who gave him sertraline. This triggered a rapid cycling episode.

He was eventually rescued by his father who took him back to Portugal where he was admitted to hospital for over a month and treated with Abilify first and Olanzapine later (dose unclear) together with Sodium Valproate at a relative low dose, 200mg or 400 mg (dose unclear).

He later had to stop Sodium Valproate because made him to drowsy. He also had to stop Abilify after a month because of erectile dysfunction. He reports undergoing a period of depression when he spent a month in bed. He later started to recuperate going to the gym, he found a new job and slowly started feeling better. He continued Sodium Valproate 200mg, in divided doses until July 2018 and eventually stopped in August because he felt low and couldn't concentrate at work.

In January 2019, when he started experiencing the first manic symptoms he went to the GP and was given Sodium Valproate 200mg, in divided dose but had bad digestive problem with diarrhoea alternated to constipation, He asked for a referral to the public sector but was told that he could be seen only in two months. Then he went to A&E and hospitalised for one night and recommended to start Abilify 10 mg, mane and to stop Sodium valproate in view of the digestive collateral effects.

**Medical history**
Nil of note. No allergies.

**Family History**
Father and mother in their 60ies. Mother possibly affected by dementia.
Younger brother tried to commit suicide at 11 ys. old. Eldest brother suffered from a depressive episode.

**Past Psychiatric History**
Patient describes himself with a cyclothymic temperament. Saw a psychologist early on as had a difficult upbringing. Works as a video-editor in London. Lives in shared household. Has a good support network of friends aware of his bipolar illness.

**Drugs & Alcohol History**
Has taken recreational drugs like MDMA, hashish and marijuana in the past. Has not touched drugs in the past 6 months as aware of negative impact on his mental state. Has not used alcohol in the past 3-4 weeks for same reasons.

**Forensic History**
Nil of note.

**Mental State Examination**
Young and slim Caucasian male well groomed, slightly overfamiliar. Visibly agitated with increased psychomotor agitation, standing up and pacing around. Speech increased in rate. Mood easily changeable, irritable at times. His thoughts are not always congruent and goal directed and present with derailment and tangentiallity. Denies abnormality of perception or any current delusional beliefs. No current risks to self or others detected during this meeting. Only risk is of further deterioration if left untreated.

**Formulation**
Manic relapse in bipolar disorder. We discussed different treatment options in terms of antipsychotic and mood stabilisers medications. He has preferred Quetiapine after hearing side effects profile.

**Plan**
I recommended to start Quetiapine XL 300mg, tonight to be increased to 600mg, nocte starting tmw night and to meet soon next week Wednesday 13/03/19 at 20.00.

---


---

## GP-Letter-Psychiatrist-A-2019-03-13

*Source: `2019/03-March/Psychiatry/GP-Letter-Psychiatrist-A-2019-03-13.md`*

# GP Letter — Psychiatrist A (London) — 13-03-2019

**Clinic Date:** 13 March 2019
**Paciente:** Patient
**Psychiatrist:** Psychiatrist A (London) — Consultant Psychiatrist
**Addressed to:** GP Surgery A (London)
**Type:** Follow-up — GP letter

---

## Verbatim Transcription

13 March 2019

Clinic Date: 13 March 2019

Dear Doctor

Re: Mr Patient [SURNAME REMOVED] - dob [DOB REMOVED]
[ADDRESS REMOVED]

I had the pleasure to meet again Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] today for a follow up appointment during my outpatients' clinic at [Clinic A (London)].

Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] was taking Quetiapine XL 600mg, nocte for a manic relapse of a bipolar disorder as per clinic letter dated 08/03/19.

Today Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] reports great improvement of his mental state and states feeling fine and stable 'very normal'. He is able to sleep a lot better without the aid of Promethazine for 8 hours per night. Also his mood has greatly normalised without any feature of irritability and without harbouring violent thoughts for the less energetic and able ones. Sexual function and libido have also reduced to baseline and he is now able to function and concentrate at work, he does not experience racing thoughts any longer. He has recently gone back to work as free-lance and he is now teaching in Brighton for few days a week. He complains of milder fluctuations of his mood however these are much more bearable than previously. His current main fear is a depressive episode which he knows it normally follows mania.

Today Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] presents much more composed and appropriate with normal levels of engagement and normal speech. Significantly calmer with no psychomotor agitation or restlessness. Mood is rated subjectively as within his normal usual range and objectively noted as slightly subdued. No delusional beliefs or abnormalities of perception are reported and no indirect signs are detected. Cognition is normal with excellent insight into his mental health needs and the need to take medications. There are no risks to self or others detected during today's meeting.

We discussed the opportunity to start a mood stabiliser as this will need to be his long term treatment strategy since it is opportune to withdraw antipsychotic medication after 4 weeks from complete resolution of psychotic symptoms as per BAP and Maudsley Guidelines. This to reduce the risk of onset of depressive episodes. Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] expresses a preference for Lamictal as mood stabiliser for its benign side effect profile.

I recommended to continue taking Quetiapine XL 600mg, nocte for the time being and to start Lamictal 25 mg, mane for 14 days and to increment 25mg, every 14 days until it reaches 100mg, mane as per BNF titration.

I would be very grateful if you could start repeat prescription for Quetiapine XL 600mg, nocte and Lamictal 25mg, mane for 14 days and if you could continue to titrate Lamictal according to BNF-that is with an increment of 25 mg every 14 days until it reaches 100mg, mane.

Should you have any queries please do not hesitate to ask.

Yours sincerely

[Psychiatrist A (London)]
Consultant Psychiatrist

---


---

## GP-Letter-Psychiatrist-A-2019-11-06

*Source: `2019/11-November/Psychiatry/GP-Letter-Psychiatrist-A-2019-11-06.md`*

# GP Letter — Psychiatrist A (London) — 06-11-2019

**Clinic Date:** 6 November 2019
**Paciente:** Patient
**Psychiatrist:** Psychiatrist A (London) — Consultant Psychiatrist
**Addressed to:** GP Surgery A (London)
**Type:** Follow-up — GP letter

---

## Verbatim Transcription

6 November 2019

Clinic Date: 6 November 2019

Dear Doctor

Re: Mr Patient [SURNAME REMOVED] - dob [DOB REMOVED]
[ADDRESS REMOVED]

I had the pleasure to meet again Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] today for a follow up appointment during my outpatients' clinic at [Clinic A (London)].

Mr [SURNAME REMOVED] is taking Quetiapine XL 300mg, nocte and Lamictal 150 mg, mane.

Patient comes back to the clinic asking for his medications to be changed to Seroquel and Lamictal instead of the generic brand. He states that he has been unstable since the last time we met in may and is unhappy about the public sector. He tells me that Seroquel was changed to immediate release and that formulation knocked him out and was unable to wake up the next day. He reports that mood has been unstable feeling more easily irritated, nervous, impatient or quick tempered. He also easily plunged into depression with poor motivation, depressed mood and frequent headaches.

He denies any angry outburst, any frank manic or psychotic symptoms.

Today he presents his usual pleasant and talking individual. His speech was normal for rate and volume. He has reactive affect and normal mood. No manic or psychotic symptoms were reported nor indirect signs were noted. He denies any thought/intention or plan to harm self or others.

We discussed how unlikely it may be that current variation in his mood and energy levels may due to the changes of the brand. I recommended him trying to transition on high dose of Lamotrigine/Lamictal or eventually trying Lithium if higher dose of Quetiapine were poorly tolerated.

For the time being her only asked for Seroquel and Lamictal to be prescribed and to evaluate at a later stage whether it was opportune to make any further change to his treatment plan.

I prescribed Patient with Seroquel XL 300mg, nocte (10 tabs) and Lamictal 150 mg, mane (10 tabs).

I would be grateful if you could continue repeat prescription for same meds: Seroquel XL 300mg, nocte and Lamictal 150 mg, mane.

Yours sincerely

[Psychiatrist A (London)]
Consultant Psychiatrist

## GP-Letter-Psychiatrist-A-2020-09-18

*Source: `2020/09-September/Psychiatry/GP-Letter-Psychiatrist-A-2020-09-18.md`*

# GP Letter — Psychiatrist A (London) — 18-09-2020

**Clinic Date:** 18 September 2020
**Letter Date:** 21 September 2020
**Paciente:** Patient
**Psychiatrist:** Psychiatrist A (London) — Consultant Psychiatrist
**Addressed to:** GP Surgery A (London)
**Type:** Follow-up (phone) — GP letter — **DISCHARGE from caseload**

---

## Verbatim Transcription

21 September 2020

Clinic Date: 18 September 2020

Dear Dr

Re: Mr Patient [SURNAME REMOVED] - dob [DOB REMOVED]
[ADDRESS REMOVED]

I had the pleasure to talk to Patient again today over the phone for a follow up appointment and as part of my outpatients' clinic at [Clinic A (London)].

At the time of our appointment Patient was taking Quetiapine XL 300mg, nocte and Lamictal at the variable dose of 250-300mg, mane. This with good effect.

He does report 6 months of well-being with overall stable mood, energy levels and functioning. He has been steady and consistent with his rhythms at work, and continues to be in a relationship with Brazilian woman that has now joined him to live together in Portugal. Describes his mood as stable and calm however has registered a bit of a drop in the month of June which has prompted him to reduce the dose of Lamictal from 300mg, mane to 250mg, mane and more recently in the month of August he reports experiencing a couple hours of high with increased speech and elated mood towards the end of the day each day. He recalls that taking Quetiapine XL 300mg, nocte did curb it down. This mood change prompted him to increase the Lamictal back again to 300mg, mane.

He believes is happy with current combination of mood. I have advised him to slightly increase Quetiapine of 50mg max 100mg, for a total of 400mg, nocte should he experience another episode of elation and leave the dose of Lamictal unchanged or engage in a slow and careful increase of Lamictal up to 400mg, OD (normally Lamictal tends to act more slowly than Quetiapine).

He reports having felt particularly low at the beg of this week but this is likely to be due to COVID infection which appears to be mild. He is experiencing some of the symptoms- fever, muscle aches and headaches – but only managed to get a test privately so unclear whether this is a COVID-related infection. He has been advised to self-isolate for 10 days which he will. He is aware of following steps should his condition deteriorate.

He is planning to go back to Portugal as he finds it more conducive to his recovery and stability also of his mental health and now that he can work remotely does not find any reason to be in London.

I was not able to complete a full assessment of his mental state over the phone; however, he sounded pleasant and engaging as usual. Reactive in affect and in good spirit with no delusional beliefs and no abnormalities of perception reported or detected. I did not detect any risk to self or others during today's conversation.

I congratulated Patient for the good work done and progress made. I believe that he is now in full recovery however he will need to continue current medications.

I confirmed current combination of medication at current dose and suggested for him to be followed up by a psychiatrist in his local area which he says he will.

I now discharge Patient from my caseload wishing him the very best for his future.

Yours sincerely

[Psychiatrist A (London)]
Consultant Psychiatrist

---

O mediastino apresenta-se na linha média exibindo normalidade morfodimensional. Normal permeabilidade e calibre das artérias pulmonares, sem sinais de TEP.

> **English translation note:**
>

>

>
> No dyspnoea or palpitations. No urinary, respiratory or GI complaints. No fever. Good general condition. Anxiety. Conscious, cooperative, oriented. Well-coloured and hydrated. Afebrile. Cardiopulmonary auscultation: Normal. BP 120/67 mmHg, HR 68 bpm.
>
> Bloods, ECG, chest X-ray ordered.
>

>
> Wells score for PE: 0 + D-dimer 600 → low probability. CT Angiography requested.
>
> **CT Angiography result:** Mediastinum midline with normal morphology. Normal patency and calibre of pulmonary arteries, **no signs of PE**. No abnormal mediastinal-hilar formations. Lung parenchyma shows no significant abnormalities — no infiltrates, consolidations, or suspicious nodules. Tracheobronchial tree normal calibre, no bronchiectasis. **No pericardial or pleural effusion.**
>
> Symptomatic treatment. Warning signs explained. Discharged.
>

# Angio TAC / TC Tórax — 06-09-2021

**Data Exame:** 06/09/2021
**Paciente:** Patient, 32 anos

## Verbatim Transcription

**RELATÓRIO:**

**TOMOGRAFIA COMPUTORIZADA TORÁCICA**
(Urgência)

**INFORMAÇÃO CLÍNICA:**

" dor torácica à esq, desde háhá 2 semanas atrás, que iniciaram apos toma de vacina..."

**TÉCNICA:**

*Exame efetuado em equipamento multidetetor de 160 cortes e tecnologia de baixa dose de radiação.* Estudo efetuado pela técnica helicoidal multicorte, com aquisição volumétrica de imagens dos vértices pulmonares ao plano das glândulas suprarrenais, durante a injeção e.v. de contraste iodado não iónico.

**RELATÓRIO:**

O mediastino apresenta-se na linha média exibindo normalidade morfodimensional. Normal permeabilidade e calibre das artérias pulmonares, sem sinais de TEP.

Não são individualizadas formações mediastino-hilares anómalas, nomeadamente de natureza adenomegálica.

A análise do parênquima pulmonar em janela densitométrica apropriada não demonstra alterações valorizáveis, nomeadamente não se observam infiltrados nem condensações parenquimatosas ou nodularidades tecidulares suspeitas de traduzir patologia evolutiva.

A árvore respiratória traqueobrônquica preserva normal calibre, sem evidência de bronquiectasias.

Ausência de derrame pericárdico ou pleural.

---

> **English translation note:**
>
> **Chest CT Angiography** (Emergency)
>
> **Clinical information:** "Left chest pain for about 2 weeks, which started after taking the vaccine..."
>
> **Technique:** 160-slice multidetector equipment with low-dose radiation. Helical multislice technique, volumetric acquisition from lung apices to adrenal glands, during IV non-ionic iodinated contrast injection.
>
> **Report:**
> - Mediastinum midline with normal morphology and dimensions
> - **Normal patency and calibre of pulmonary arteries, no signs of PE (pulmonary embolism)**
> - No abnormal mediastinal-hilar formations, namely no lymphadenopathy
> - Lung parenchyma shows no significant abnormalities — no infiltrates, consolidations, or suspicious tissue nodules
> - Tracheobronchial tree normal calibre, no bronchiectasis
> - **No pericardial or pleural effusion**
>
> **Conclusion: Normal chest CT angiography. No PE, no myocarditis signs on CT.**
